Foreign Important Telegrams 2

Japanese Government and Public Oppose, Eastern Newspaper Claims It is a Misconception and Distortion 52

▲ Tokyo, November 3 (Japan Allied News) - After the Lytton Report was released, newspapers such as Asahi, Hochi, and Nichi-Nichi severely criticized it this morning, calling it a report of misconception, distortion, insufficient understanding, disrespect, and foolishness. What it said was an exaggerated and delusional dream. They also revealed articles stating that Japan should withdraw from the League of Nations. The House of Peers and various political parties also expressed opinions criticizing the investigation team's lack of understanding.

▲ Tokyo, November 3 (Reuters) - Today, all newspapers are paying attention to the Lytton Report and have no time to care about other matters, and all unanimously express dissatisfaction, but the general tone is still mild.

▲ Tokyo, November 3 (Den Tsushin) - Regarding the Lytton Report, which is viewed as an attempt to judge the Far Eastern issue, the Tokyo Asahi Shimbun published an editorial today stating that those who dominated the minds of the members of the investigation team consistently based their arguments on the withdrawal of troops, regardless of the circumstances, which is nothing more than the theory of the League of Nations and has fallen into the error of what they call "disregarding the realizer." As for the principles and conditions for a solution, the advocacy of international cooperation is even more empty talk that disregards history. What authority is there to ask for such a solution?

Cabinet Meeting Today to Decide Attitude 53

▲ Tokyo, November 3 (China United Press) - Since the release of the Lytton Report, the Japanese government and public have been greatly angered. In addition to Foreign Minister Uchida and Army Minister Araki issuing statements last night, the Japanese government has not yet expressed its attitude. It is reported that a cabinet meeting will be convened tomorrow to discuss the measures, and then a statement will be issued in the name of the Tokyo government. The main points of Japan's dissatisfaction are roughly as follows: (1) The Lytton Report does not recognize the Japanese military's actions as self-defense; (2) It does not recognize that the independence of the puppet organization is due to the free will of the people of the Northeast; (3) It recognizes that sovereignty still belongs to China and does not recognize the various facts created by Japanese military power; (4) It opposes various solutions proposed by the investigation team.

Japan Ignores Investigation Report 54

Plans to Draft an Opinion Paper to Refute it

Willing to Sever Ties with the League of Nations

▲ Tokyo, November 3 (Reuters) - A Foreign Ministry spokesman said this morning that the Japanese government plans to only briefly touch upon the last few chapters of the Lytton Report, as "Manchukuo" has already been recognized and there is no need to comment on it in detail. Japan's opinion paper can be drafted in about two or three weeks.

▲ Tokyo, November 3 (Den Tsushin) - The report of the investigation team, which is viewed as an attempt to judge the Far Eastern issue, was officially released at 9:00 PM yesterday. The Japanese government authorities decided that the contents of the report were too inappropriate and had deviated from the original mission of the investigation team, so they decided to submit an opinion paper to the League of Nations Council on November 4 to refute it in detail. The authorities have established a joint committee of the Foreign Ministry and the Army to start drafting. It is reported that the Japanese government's policy on the opinion paper is roughly as follows: (1) The mission of the investigation team, as resolved by the League of Nations Council on December 10 last year, does not have legal binding force on the League of Nations General Assembly and only provides reference materials. It is hoped that the League of Nations will not be bound by the report and will adapt to the new situation on the ground to seek appropriate solutions. (2) Chapters 1, 2, 3, 7, and 8 of the report mainly describe facts, and there are generally no objections, but Chapter 4 describes the Manchurian situation after September 18, Chapter 5 describes the Shanghai Incident, and Chapter 6 states that "Manchukuo" cannot be recognized by the Japanese government. (3) Chapter 9 on the arguments and conditions for a solution and Chapter 10 on the conclusion are not considered by the Japanese government, which has recognized "Manchukuo" as an independent country. In particular, the proposal to establish a demilitarized zone with the organization of a gendarmerie under the cooperation of international instructors as a condition for not recognizing the autonomous occurrence and growth of Manchukuo is a proposal that completely exceeds the mission of the investigation team, and the Japanese government absolutely cannot recognize it. (4) Although the Japanese government has no intention of automatically inducing the worst-case scenario to seek to withdraw from the alliance, if the alliance continues its lack of understanding, it has the intention of severing ties with the alliance and moving towards an independent solution to the Far Eastern issue. This must be stated.

▲ Tokyo, November 3 (Reuters) - The general opinion in Japan is that the suggestions for resolving the Manchurian case in the Lytton Report, if proposed half a year ago, would have been acceptable to Japan, but today the independence of the new country has already been completed, and it is impossible to accept it. Furthermore, officials here believe that the best policy for the League of Nations is to wait two or three years for "Manchukuo" to have the opportunity to prove its ability and security. After this period expires, the League of Nations can decide which is better, autonomy under China or outright independence, especially since the Chinese government itself is also unstable.

Political Parties Issue Arrogant Statements 55

▲ Tokyo, November 3 (Den Tsushin) - The Seiyukai issued the following statement by President Suzuki today regarding the Lytton Report: The Lytton Report's proposed solution to the Sino-Japanese dispute is nothing more than a castle in the air, because it does not conform to the reality of the Far East, so it is impossible to implement. Even if it could be implemented, the situation would be worse than what led to the September 18th Incident. It is sufficient for the three countries of China, Japan, and Russia to resolve the issue, and if the League of Nations is involved, things will become more complicated and confusing. However, the life and death relationship of the realistic Japan and the national sentiment cannot be ignored by any country in the world.

▲ Tokyo, November 3 (Den Tsushin) - The Minseito issued the following statement regarding the report: The Lytton Report expresses a surprising lack of understanding. The fact that the central government of China has no real power to govern Manchuria is a clear fact, so Manchuria is a breeding ground for bandits and red movements, and the Lytton Committee wants to return those who have no ability to govern to the status of sovereign, which will only make Manchuria a lane of turmoil again, both domestically and internationally.

Japanese Navy Determined to Resist the US 56

▲ Tokyo, November 3 (China United Press) - After the Japanese government received the Lytton Report, it was very embarrassed. It is reported that the Japanese Navy Department has decided to replenish its naval strength and has decided to use a new budget of 500 million Japanese yen to build new warships and various new weapons in preparation for actively resisting the US. The Japanese Ministry of Finance, due to the firm attitude of the Navy Department, has agreed to negotiate separately to meet its demands.

Observations from Geneva 57

Saying it can consider both law and facts

▲Havas Agency, Geneva, 2nd. A special correspondent for Le Temps of Paris claims that those in charge at the League of Nations believe the Lytton Report is able to consider both law and facts. For example, the report explains that the "Manchukuo" is not an organization automatically created by residents, and advocates for maintaining Chinese sovereignty in Manchuria, all of which are points based on legal arguments. As for the facts, the report fully acknowledges that Japan's rights in Manchuria have indeed been damaged. The report also repeatedly explains and proposes a solution that advocates for close cooperation between China and Japan within a certain territorial range. Within this territory, China would have its sovereignty, its administration would be autonomous, and Japan's special rights within this territory would also need to be fully recognized. As for the rights of various foreign countries within Manchuria, the investigation team concluded that the Open Door Policy should be maintained. All of these are based on factual considerations.

▲National News Agency, Geneva, 3rd. People at the League of Nations have mixed feelings about the Lytton Report, with some offering commentary. They believe that the investigation team's recommendations are tantamount to abandoning the League of Nations' obligations and promises. Regarding Article 10 of the Covenant, which guarantees the complete territorial integrity of each member state, this situation is particularly obvious. They fear that some small countries, wanting to avoid creating the most dangerous precedent for themselves, will vigorously oppose the proposed solution. However, some believe that we cannot prejudge that Japan will definitely violate the principles of the League of Nations. Therefore, even if Japan, according to the investigation team's plan, can obtain a very large sphere of influence in Manchuria, it is not fundamentally strange that it still does not agree to internationalize Manchuria in this way. In short, observers here all believe that future discussions on the Lytton Report at the League of Nations are likely to provoke extremely complex and difficult negotiations between Japan and the major powers.

▲Reuters, Geneva, 2nd. It is generally expected that the scope of the conference on the clear questions presented in the Lytton Report has been clearly defined. Therefore, the point that China previously opposed direct negotiations with Japan should be eliminated. As for the various proposals contained in the report, it is generally believed that Japan may not necessarily agree to withdraw all armed forces except for the constabulary. It is also believed that Japan may not necessarily agree to completely change the current situation in the three northeastern provinces and implement a new system of autonomy within the framework of Chinese sovereignty and administrative integrity. The general opinion is that this report is the most noteworthy document published by a group under the auspices of the League of Nations. Its narration and arguments are prudent and moderate, and the writing style is elegant, clearly showing an English style. From its wording, it seems that every part was written by Lytton himself, but it is obvious that some parts were inserted later. This report can be regarded as an indictment of the Japanese.

▲International Telegraph Agency, Geneva, 2nd. Yesterday, Sunday, hundreds of reporters from various countries gathered in the League of Nations press room, quietly waiting for the publication of the Lytton Report. Everyone recognizes that this report is of extremely great importance. The report contains thousands of words that criticize Japanese militarism and judge that the Japanese military's seizure of Shenyang on the night of September 18th, using the excuse of self-defense, was improper. The section in the report that demands the withdrawal of Japanese troops from Manchuria can obtain strong support from various small countries because they fear that Japan's actions will be imitated, endangering their own future independence and security. Furthermore, French Premier Herriot's attitude has formed a consensus in Geneva. According to Herriot, France does not take sides between China and Japan, but Europe must maintain the League of Nations Covenant and various treaties in the Far East. This not only concerns the interests of the League of Nations but also has a great impact on world peace.

▲Reuters, Geneva, 3rd. Now that all sectors have the opportunity to leisurely study the Lytton Report, it is now possible to express opinions more completely and from a broader perspective. Although the first impression seems to indicate that the report is entirely unfavorable to Japan and protects the Chinese side, there are currently many divergent opinions, which must be acknowledged. For example, various sectors in Poland said that the resolutions in the report are slightly far-fetched or too circuitous based on their premises. They believe that the evidence collected by the investigation team is indeed very helpful to the Japanese side, but its resolutions are unfavorable to Japan. The report has shown that China is not currently in a position to restore order or reorganize to return to normalcy. They also said that the investigation team even admitted that it is impossible to restore the old situation in the three northeastern provinces, and some even said that recognizing Japan's special economic and financial interests proves the legitimacy of its special actions. Other European opinions believe that the report may be the basis for a coordinated solution, especially the conditions for granting autonomy to the new government of Manchuria. However, the majority opinion regards the report as a solemn and practical plan formulated based on a prudent, complete, and objective investigation, indicating that although Japan has legitimate hopes in terms of economy and security, there is really no way to find a solution except based on Chinese sovereignty.

Various Opinions of British Newspapers 58

▲Reuters, London, 3rd. The Manchester Guardian stated that the Lytton Report was painstakingly drafted with gentle and reasonable wording. If it makes Japanese behavior more understandable, it also makes it more detestable. The world must not allow Japan to achieve its main purpose of destroying the credibility of the League of Nations by recognizing "Manchukuo." The newspaper agrees with the investigation team's view that Japan's current success in the three northeastern provinces is not a blessing for Japan itself because it has created resentment, especially China's eternal hatred of Japan, which is extremely unfavorable to Japan's future. The newspaper also said that if China's demands for its treaty rights, such as the credibility of the League of Nations Covenant and the Kellogg-Briand Pact, fall in the Far East, they will be despised everywhere in the world.

▲Reuters, London, 3rd. Today, all London newspapers have criticisms regarding the Lytton Report. The Times editorial stated that the principles of the Lytton Report are not difficult to acknowledge, but the time elapsed between the drafting of the report and its delivery to Geneva has unfortunately made the report's conclusions seem to have been damaged by this time gap. Furthermore, the investigation team's departure was slightly delayed, and its return was before Japan recognized "Manchukuo," which was also a disadvantage for the investigation team. The investigation team's task was originally to investigate the facts of Shenyang, but the investigation team did not arrive in the Far East until five months after the incident. What the League of Nations and the United States are now encountering is a variation of the three northeastern provinces becoming a Japanese protectorate. The report suggests a solution that, in the investigation team's view, can be applied to the situation in the three northeastern provinces that they saw, and gives full understanding to Japan's special political and economic interests. Therefore, the proposals it drafted are not suitable for the legitimate form of an arbitrator but are suitable for the wisdom of friends of both China and Japan. Considering today's environment, can this kind of proposal be immediately realized in practice? This is the question. There is absolutely no doubt that Tokyo will not be willing to accept these proposals, but the Lytton team is sure that the public opinion in the three northeastern provinces is against Japan. Japan is now in great difficulty, its financial resources are unable to maintain the cost of continuing military operations, and its people may eventually express sympathy for the Lytton Report and believe that ignoring the public opinion in the three northeastern provinces can never be a blessing for Japan. Foreign governments will certainly need some time to study the significance of this report. It is not appropriate to make hasty decisions, and there must be collective rather than individual diplomatic actions. The League of Nations Administrative Council may not be able to discuss this report before next month. The report does not support the League of Nations' propaganda that accuses the Japanese side of infringing on the rights of weaker countries. The proposals in the report seek to solve this problem while maintaining the dignity of both China and Japan. Unfortunately, international success is unlikely because Japan believes that the Manchurian problem has already been solved. The conclusion of the report is that China must have a strong central government. This level is still a major obstacle to the solution. If the solution must wait for China's internal construction and the result of international cooperation, there will be a long wait. Although Japan's actions in the three northeastern provinces are inappropriate, Chinese politics also contributed to them. The Morning Post paid attention to the point in the report about building a strong government in China and stated that China's future is feared to disintegrate. Therefore, saying that the Republic of China is the ruler of China is just a "courtesy title." If Japan and other countries can cooperate to rebuild a strong central government in China, it can be said to be a great success. But whether this plan can be realized is questionable. As for the construction proposals of the investigation team, they must actually be realized through several years of meetings. It seems difficult to establish them in the current environment. The newspaper advocates that Foreign Secretary Simon should not support any actions that would promote Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations because Japan's withdrawal would cause various disputes, and Japan's presence in the three northeastern provinces is actually the same in nature as Britain's presence in India and Egypt. The Westminster Gazette calls on Prime Minister MacDonald to reassert his influence in diplomacy. If the MacDonald government only adopts a wait-and-see attitude and does not take immediate action, the credibility of the current government will be greatly affected.

Chilean Civil War Ends 62

▲Havas, Rio de Janeiro, 3rd. The São Paulo rebels in Chile have now surrendered unconditionally. Major Silva received the São Paulo government in the name of the Chilean Federal Government.

Telegram

Chiang Kai-shek's circular telegram to the Shanghai Municipal Government, copied to all newspaper offices: Under orders, Zhongzheng is stationed in Wuhan to supervise the suppression of the Red bandits. Fortunately, with the unity and cooperation of the military and civilians, we have worked hard to gradually eliminate them. However, in the recovered areas, everything has been exhausted, there is no house that has not been burned, no tree that has not been felled, no chicken or dog left, and no plowing cattle that have not been killed. According to reports from front-line generals in the past half month, places such as Shangcheng, Guangshan, and Gushi in Henan; Liu'an, Jinzhai, Yingshan, and Huoshan in Anhui; and Huang'an, Macheng, Luotian, Mianyang, and Jianli in Hubei are all like wasteland. The land is desolate, no smoke is seen, only wild cries are heard, and even thousands upon thousands of people kneel before the army, with emaciated faces, lying stiffly on the roadside. After reading these reports, Zhongzheng was angry and saddened. He has telegraphed the governments of the three provinces to rush to provide disaster relief and food relief, and to send personnel to provide assistance. He has also promulgated measures to reduce and exempt land taxes in bandit suppression areas for compliance to provide stability. However, the recovered areas have been sinking for a long time, the disasters are deep, there are many people waiting to be relieved, the areas waiting to be relieved are even wider, the food for relief is limited, and the funds for relief are extremely small. Soon autumn will end and winter will come, and it is unbearable to imagine the deaths from freezing and starvation. Zhongzheng deeply believes that when hunger and cold reach the body, even a loving mother cannot protect her child, and from ancient times, famine has been followed by great chaos. After the great chaos is quelled, it must be followed by famine, which are mutually causal. If we do not properly plan for the aftermath, the stability of the local area and the restoration of order will never be possible. Therefore, I hope that all people's organizations, charitable institutions, and wealthy households will do their best to collect large sums of money for relief, and report the amount collected to this headquarters for verification and dispatch. It must be known that in these days of multiple disasters, if we want to save ourselves, we must first save others. If the country is not peaceful, where can the home be safe? We must also know that saving people is not entirely from the idea of ​​alleviating suffering, but is actually a normal duty. We will make the people who violate the law have hope of rebirth, equalize happiness and suffering, and make society have a chance to recover. Fortune, misfortune, safety, and danger are indeed shared with the people of the whole country. Furthermore, there is another thing to be said. Since the military campaign began, not only has the chaos been more severe than in the past, but the honesty has also been inferior to the past. Cities are becoming more and more extravagant, while rural areas are suffering more and more. If this continues to develop day by day, even without foreign troubles, how can we avoid destruction? I hope that all school and organization leaders and women's organizations will form inspection teams to visit the disaster areas in batches to understand the truth and plan for relief. This headquarters will pay attention to protecting and facilitating their inspection process so that the whole country, from top to bottom, will be aware of this tragedy, commonly advocate simplicity, strive to curb extravagance, restore the countryside, and promote the sales of agricultural products as a common goal and path for our people. I hope that you will carefully consider this. Chiang Kai-shek, 30th year of the Republic of China, printed

Recent Bombings in Tianjin 64

▲Four incidents in one night

▲May be related to the sale of Japanese goods

Tianjin Correspondence: Yesterday (29th) at 6:40 PM, someone placed a bomb on the right side of the glass window in front of Renchang Thread Store (i.e. foreign goods store) on Dongma Road. As it was near dusk and the market was gradually becoming lively, no one noticed the person who placed the bomb. When the colleagues at Renchang discovered it and were about to shout and warn, the bomb went off with a loud bang, and smoke filled the streets. Pedestrians were alarmed and fled in panic, and order was disrupted as a result. Shops closed their doors one after another. Zhang Keming, the 17th guard police officer of the Fourth Precinct in the area, blew his whistle to notify nearby posts to be on alert, and returned to the precinct to report. At 7:00 PM, the military police, security team, and police arrived one after another and immediately cut off traffic to search, but nothing was found. Traffic was restored at 7:30 PM. Unexpectedly, order had just been restored when bomb incidents occurred at Huazhu Woolen Store and Ruifuxiang Silk Store (also foreign goods) on Gu Yi Street, and at the Zhongyuan Company in the Japanese Concession. According to a staff member at Huazhu Store, at 7:35 PM, a rickshaw was speeding west with a young man about 20 years old wearing a dark blue cloth gown and a felt hat. As he passed the front of Huazhu's door, he threw something inside. The staff member knew something was wrong and was about to chase the person who threw the object, but a loud noise suddenly erupted in the store, making them stunned. After a while, when they regained consciousness, the rickshaw had disappeared. After investigation, Wu Zilun, a staff member at Renchang Store, was slightly injured in the face and more severely injured in the legs. Cui Hongkui, a pedestrian, was injured in his right leg, and Zhao Desan was injured in his left leg. The bomb shell flew to Fuxingcheng Leather Goods Store across the street, where Zheng San, an apprentice at the store, was injured in the throat and fainted on the spot with blood gushing out. He was sent to the Municipal Hospital, where he died shortly after. At Huazhu Store, Fei Runxuan, who served as an accountant and acting manager, was injured in the right eye and right leg. Jin Ruisheng, a staff member, was injured in both legs. Lu Shaoting was injured in the forehead, and Wang Shiqi, an apprentice, was injured in the back, and his condition was very serious. At 9:00 PM, Wang Yimin, the director of the Public Security Bureau, led special agents and police to Huazhu Store to inspect. A light yellow wooden handle was found inside Huazhu Store, proving that the object thrown was a hand grenade with a diameter of about four inches and a very strong explosive force. As for the situation at Ruifuxiang after the bombing, the store kept it strictly confidential. Neighbors said that they heard a loud bang, but it was not very loud, and it seemed to be a small bomb. Someone secretly placed a bomb in the piece goods department on the third floor of the Zhongyuan Company in the Japanese Concession. Fortunately, it did not explode. The store staff was very frightened after reporting the incident to the Japanese police station, who took the bomb away. That evening, each newspaper office received a public letter from the "Dare to Die Corps to Eliminate Traitors Behind the Front Lines," explaining the bombing situation and saying that there were more than 30 people working in Tianjin. If the unscrupulous merchants do not arouse their patriotic conscience again, there will be further treatment. (September 30th)

▲Communist Bandits Plan Riot on Double Tenth Festival

They are also opening clothing stores so that tailors can get close to women in military and political circles to spy on military intelligence. They are dispatching henchmen to enlist in the army, engaging in military transport or plotting assassinations. The Public Security Bureau has also ordered each branch bureau to pay attention to newly opened small businesses within its jurisdiction.

Regarding the number of people, all newly opened businesses must seek a guarantor and specify the location of relocation for verification. Special attention must be paid to unfamiliar faces. After nightfall, military police and armed police from the Public Security Bureau will patrol in sections, and plainclothes detectives will be secretly dispatched to observe passersby. Anyone with suspicious behavior will be checked and questioned. The arrangements for maintaining city security are unusually strict. (September 28th)

The Course of Japanese Seizure of the Chinese Eastern Railway 66

▲Expanding Influence by Manipulating Puppet Organizations

▲Conflict with Soviet Russia Intensifies

The Chinese Eastern Railway was built thirty years ago by old Russia to invade the Far East and gain an outlet to the ocean, connecting the east with the Pacific Ocean. The completion of this railway greatly impacted Japan's coveting of Manchuria and Mongolia, leading to the Russo-Japanese War. Ultimately, Russia was defeated by Japan, ceding the section south of Changchun to Dalian to Japan, which was named the South Manchuria Railway. Since then, the Chinese Eastern Railway has been centered on Harbin, with the western line running from Manchuria Station to Harbin, the eastern line running from Ha East to Suifenhe on the Sino-Russian border, and the southern line running from Ha to Changchun. The entire line is 1,721 kilometers long. The railway passes through Manchuria Station into Russia, connecting with the Baikal-Amur Mainline, reaching Moscow and various European countries, becoming a direct route between Europe and Asia. The eastern line passes through Suifenhe into Russia, connecting with the Ussuri Railway, reaching Vladivostok and the Pacific Ocean. The southern line passes through Changchun to Dalian, entering the Yellow Sea. This railway connects Europe, Asia, the Pacific Ocean, and the Yellow Sea on three sides, and its impact on the economic development and military transportation of North and South Manchuria, the cultural communication between China, Japan, Russia, and various European countries, and the political changes in China, Japan, and Russia is extremely significant. Although this railway is nominally a Sino-Russian joint venture, it is in fact controlled and manipulated by the Russians in all aspects. The Chinese hold only nominal positions with no authority to intervene in anything. Since 1917, China has gradually taken back the rights attached to the railway to encroach on our country, including the right to protect the railway, military power, railway police power, municipal police power, judicial power, municipal administration power, navigation power, land rights, and education rights. The railway only managed train operation and transportation matters. After May 31, 1924, China and Russia signed the Outline of the Provisional Agreement on the Management of the Chinese Eastern Railway, and the Feng-Soviet Agreement was signed on September 20 of the same year. The contents of these two agreements greatly harmed China's rights. The railway was nominally a joint venture, and Article 5 of the agreement stipulated that Chinese and Russian personnel should be equally distributed, but in fact, it was just a formality. Although China sent supervisors to oversee everything, all supervisors failed to fully implement the two agreements. This is because the Russians still adhered to the traditional thinking of aggression, and all systems, regulations, organizations, and texts of the Chinese Eastern Railway still followed the Russian organizational law, without being the same as the railway organization habits of China. Therefore, although China had sent experts to manage the railway (such as Wang Jingchun, who was the supervisor of the railway in 1922 and 1923 and hired many students studying in Europe and the United States), they were restricted by habits and were not proficient in Russian, so they could not implement the management of the railway. The Chinese side only placed more personnel, and the government only got extra profits every year. As for the management of train operation, the fare of passengers and goods, the conversion of gold rubles, and all important matters, the Russians were in charge of everything, and the Chinese side just watched it succeed.

Last year, after the September 18th Incident, when Ma Zhanshan fought fiercely with the Japanese army's Duomen Division on the Tao'ang Railway, Soviet Foreign Minister Karakhan protested to Japanese Ambassador to Russia Hirota, saying that the Japanese army should not cross the Chinese Eastern Railway line under any circumstances. Later, the Ma army was defeated and retreated, and the Japanese army ignored the Soviet protests and crossed the Chinese Eastern Railway line at Ang'angxi Station (it is said that Japan had obtained the understanding of the Soviet Union) and reached the capital of Heilongjiang Province. In January of this year, the Japanese army forcibly boarded a Chinese Eastern Railway train at Kuanchengzi Station (about ten miles from Changchun, the last station on the southern line of the Chinese Eastern Railway) and wanted to go north to Harbin. The Russian stationmaster refused to start the train, and the Japanese army shot and killed several Soviet and Chinese staff members and forcibly started the train. Although the Soviet consul in Harbin protested, it was of no use. The Japanese army drove to Shuangchengpu and fought with the troops of Ding Chao and Li Du, so the southern line was not open to traffic for more than ten days due to the war, causing great damage. On February 5th of this year, the Japanese army attacked and entered Harbin, and since then, the Japanese forces have completely reached northern Manchuria. At that time, the chief of the Japanese special agency, Doihara, had completely taken over or closed all Chinese agencies, such as the mayor of Harbin, and replaced him with the traitor Bao Guancheng. The director of the Binjiang Municipal Office was replaced by Zhao Bojun, the brother of the traitor Zhao Zhongren. The chairman of the Northeast Shipping Bureau was replaced by Ying Jihua. The traitor Zhang Jinghui, because he had contacted the Japanese earlier, was retained to serve later and continued to be the chief executive of the Eastern Special Zone. All other administrative, financial, educational, industrial, newspaper, and other agencies were changed or the Japanese were sent as advisors. Only the Chinese personnel of the Chinese Eastern Railway have not been changed, and the Japanese have not intervened because they want to think about the Soviet Union's attitude.

Since the Japanese forces have reached northern Manchuria, they must want to take a share of the Chinese Eastern Railway. How could they not seize the rights of the Chinese side? However, the Japanese are still wary of the Soviet Union and dare not act rashly. On March 9th, the puppet state was established, and the traitor Puyi took office, so he intervened in the Chinese Eastern Railway and changed all the senior cadres of the Chinese side. This matter has a great relationship with the conflict between Japanese and Russian forces. I will describe it in detail. From the beginning, the annexation of the three northeastern provinces by the Japanese has not been supported by the countries of the world, especially the Soviet Union. This is an undeniable fact, so the Japanese have never dared to seize the rights of the Chinese Eastern Railway in a decisive manner like they seized purely Chinese agencies. The highest organ of the Chinese Eastern Railway is the board of directors, and the chairman of the board is concurrently held by the Chinese supervisor, with five Chinese and five Russian directors. Among the five Chinese directors, one is the chairman, and among the five Russian directors, one is the vice chairman. At this time, the Chinese Eastern Railway supervisor and chairman of the board was Mo Dehui. Because Mo was in Moscow and had not returned, his position was temporarily taken by Li Shaogeng. After the puppet state was established, the South Manchuria Railway strongly advocated that Lü Ronghuan should be the supervisor. Lü was the former supervisor, and the strongest advocate for Lü was the director of the South Manchuria Railway Office, Utsaku Umi. At the same time, the Japanese military部方面 advocated that a moderate attitude should be adopted towards the Soviet Union, because Lü still had traces of not being able to reach a compromise with the Soviet Union during the Sino-Soviet conflict in 1929. Li Shaogeng had real estate in Harbin worth more than one million, and he was very addicted to being an official and was afraid that his property would be confiscated if he was not an official for a day, so he contacted Uze Seishi, the director of the Eastern Railway Library, to run and campaign for him with the Japanese and the puppet state authorities. Uze was an old student of the Japanese Imperial University and was a member of the old National Assembly. He was one of the four great guardians of the Anfu faction when it was in power. He was a banner man and had a close relationship with Puyi, so he ran for Li Shaogeng. After Li became the supervisor, Uze jumped to become a counselor. (To be continued)

Central Party Headquarters Commemoration Week 67

▲He Yingqin Speaks on How to Restore National Spirit and Status

At 9 a.m. on the 3rd, the Nanjing Office of the Central Party Headquarters held the Premier's Commemoration Week. Ye Chucang, Ju Zheng, Gu Mengyu, He Yingqin, He Yaozu, Zhang Daofan, Chen Zhaoying, and other staff members attended. After Gu Mengyu presided over the ceremony, He Yingqin reported on how to restore national spirit and status, saying that he would speak from the Premier's words on nationalism, "China is foolishly dreaming of relying solely on others." He stated that if we do not remove this foolish dreaming, the nation's future is extremely dangerous. We can only rely on ourselves and start with active preparation. The first step is to cultivate a great future from a spirit of peace, which means that the people must have healthy bodies and minds. Only after popularizing national physical education can we talk about resistance, survival, and competition. Last time, when conscripting the military police, only 25% of those examined were healthy. From this, it can be seen that no more than half of the Chinese population is completely healthy. Moreover, the mortality rate is too high, and the population is at risk of gradually decreasing. This is all because of a lack of attention to physical education and hygiene. It can also be said that education has failed, leading to a failure to popularize physical education and only creating a group of weak scholars. In the future, we must actively consolidate our national defense with the goal of self-defense, and we must quickly cultivate and improve the people's physical fitness. Therefore, I believe that the promotion of physical education and the establishment of hygiene facilities are extremely important. With national spirit, there will naturally be national status. In this way, the future of China will definitely be very promising.

Ministry of Finance Revises Banknote Issuance Tax 68

▲Tax Rate Revised to 1.25%

▲Tax Law Currently Being Reviewed by the Legislative Yuan

The Executive Yuan, based on the revised Banknote Issuance Tax Law submitted by the Ministry of Finance, was brought up at the 66th Executive Yuan meeting on the 23rd of last month, passed, and sent to the Legislative Yuan. On the 1st of this month, the Legislative Yuan meeting decided to hand it over to the Finance and Economic Committees for review. The contents of the Ministry of Finance's submission to the Executive Yuan and the draft amendment are recorded below:

▲Original Submission from the Ministry of Finance: The Banknote Issuance Tax Law was promulgated by the National Government on August 1, 1931, and the articles were copied and distributed by your esteemed Yuan on August 12 of the same year, ordering compliance. In accordance with this, the Ministry prepared for collection and ordered the issuing banks to comply with the tax rate. Subsequently, the China Communications Bank, the Zhongnan Bank, the Siming Bank, the China Industrial Bank, the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the China Reclamation Bank, and the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank jointly submitted a report, stating that according to the regulations of the Banknote Issuance Tax Law, the issuance tax should be paid at 2.5% of the 40% guarantee reserve, etc. After joint discussion and consultation, it was unanimously agreed that the issuance tax would affect the finances of the banks, and even though they had already assumed the burden, the Shanghai Banking Association submitted a reply on September 11, 1931. This matter has been put aside for years, and disasters have multiplied, and financial exhaustion has reached its peak. It is not easy to maintain and adjust. If heavy taxes are imposed again, it will directly affect the affairs of the banks and indirectly affect the national finances. The burden of each bank at this time is indeed painful. If this causes financial contraction, the result is unbearable. All kinds of difficulties have been repeatedly presented through elected representatives. Now, I will reiterate it to your esteemed ministry. Looking at the meager tax system of various countries, the benefits to the government are small, while the adjustment of currency is great. If we collect taxes at the current tax rate, I am afraid that finance will become tighter, which would lose the effect of adjustment and promote the proliferation of foreign currency. Furthermore, in terms of the banks themselves, since the January 28 Incident, their vitality has not recovered, and all industries have declined. It is undeniable that they are relying on finance for maintenance. If heavy taxes are imposed now, the banks can only take compensation from various industries, otherwise, they will inevitably shrink their loans, and the market will suffer. Moreover, the issuing banks all follow the prices set by the ministry when investing in guarantee reserve bonds. The national crisis suddenly occurred, and bond prices plummeted, and the accumulated losses from reorganization were also unaffordable. The smallness of the profit does not need to be stated clearly. I only hope that your esteemed ministry will take into account the overall planning of government affairs. At this time, the national treasury is extraordinarily short, and it is entirely reliant on opening up tax sources to help. Our banks have always relied on your protection. No matter how difficult it is, if it is within our power, we should take both into account and use our soil to help you. However, the tax rate of 2.5%

is really an excessive burden that the banks cannot bear. We can only truthfully ask your esteemed ministry to sympathize with the difficulties of businesses and consider the suffering of the people, and to give further consideration to quickly reduce the previously determined tax rate to no more than 1.25% of the guarantee reserve, and to quickly submit it to the Executive Yuan for consultation with the Legislative Yuan to revise the tax rate to relieve the hardships of businesses. According to the profit and loss reports sent by the banks at the end of last year, the China Bank had a net profit of more than 1,837,400 yuan, and the China Communications Bank had a net profit of more than 787,500 yuan. The China Bank should pay a tax of more than 1,535,574 yuan, and the China Communications Bank should pay a tax of more than 622,690 yuan. In comparison, the annual net profit of the two largest banks, China and Communications, is almost entirely used to pay taxes, and the others can be seen even more. It is true that the banks claim that the burden is too heavy and that they are unable to bear it. It is appropriate to reduce it to 1.25% of the guarantee reserve. It seems appropriate to approve the request in order to both benefit the national treasury and show concern for the hardships of businesses. In addition, the articles of other articles of the law are either slightly unclear or there are obstacles to implementation. They should be revised in accordance with the facts and principles in order to ensure that the law is established and the order is carried out without contradiction. In addition to approving the submission and requesting that the tax money for the 21st year still be paid according to the original tax rate, the reasons for revising the Banknote Issuance Tax Law are reasonably compiled into a clear memorandum and respectfully submitted to your esteemed Yuan for review and humbly request to transfer to the Legislative Yuan for review and request for promulgation and implementation.

▲Contents of the Amendment (1) Banks that are specially permitted to issue exchange coupons shall pay the exchange coupon issuance tax in accordance with the Issuance Tax Law. (2) The exchange coupon issuance tax shall be paid at the same rate for silver yuan coupons and transfer currency coupons. Subsidiary currency coupons shall be calculated at ten jiao per yuan. (3) Banks issuing exchange coupons shall have a 100% reserve, with at least 60% as cash reserve and the remainder as guarantee reserve. The cash reserve portion shall be exempt from the issuance tax. (4) Banks issuing exchange coupons shall fill in the issuance number and the number of cash guarantee reserves separately in accordance with the semi-monthly report form set by the Ministry of Finance and report them truthfully. The Ministry of Finance shall register the reported numbers separately on a semi-monthly basis and calculate the average number for twelve months after one year. (5) The tax rate for the exchange coupon issuance tax shall be set at 1.25% of the actual guarantee reserve amount for collection. (6) The exchange coupon issuance tax shall be collected at the beginning of each fiscal year according to the average number of the previous year. (7) After receiving the collection notice from the Ministry of Finance, banks that should pay the exchange coupon issuance tax shall pay it within ten days through the local central bank, obtain a receipt, and submit it to the Ministry of Finance for verification. (8) If a bank does not comply with the Issuance Tax Law to pay the exchange coupon issuance tax, the Ministry of Finance may revoke its special issuance right. (9) If the Ministry of Finance considers the matters reported by the bank to be untrue, it may send personnel to inspect the issuance account and the reserve account. If there is indeed any concealment or underreporting, in addition to ordering payment, a fine of more than 500 yuan and less than 3,000 yuan shall be imposed. (10) Banks issuing exchange coupons shall pay the tax payable on the exchange coupons used by other banks together, but may recover it from the using bank.

Travel Notes to the West (III) (X) (I) 69

(2) Quanzigou Coal Mine: This mine is located 63 li north of the county, about 3 li northwest of Shangyu Village. About 1 li northwest from Shangyu Village, the geological changes on the west bank of the Yellow River are extremely drastic, and faults and folds are quite complex. Ordovician limestone near the river is covered by the Carboniferous Permian coal system. Only near Quanzigou, the rock layers are flat and there are no changes. A horizontal adit is used to mine coal. The height of the adit is 3.5 to 5 feet, and the width is 3 to 4 feet. The length is about 160 zhang. The coal seam is about 6 feet thick. According to the foreman, this is the thickest part of the third coal seam, about 30 feet. This time, all three wells have not been seen. It is thought that it is a local change. The second coal seam is about 20 feet away from the second layer and is about 2 feet thick. The third coal seam is about 50 feet away from the first coal seam and the layer is about 1 foot thick. The strike is southeast and northwest, and the dip is from 0 to 5 degrees. The wood used for the coal lane pillars is about 3 to 4 inches in diameter. Three pieces of wood are used for each frame. The two sides of the stone lane are built with waste stone. There are very few places where wood is used for support. Each digger must dig 36 baskets of coal per shift. The wage is 300 copper coins. Each hauler is paid 12 copper coins for each basket hauled. Each person can haul 30 to 40 baskets per day. Each basket contains about 130 jin of coal. Food and lamp oil are provided by the workers themselves. The foreman earns 6 yuan a month. Food and lamp oil are provided by the mine owner. Each person needs about 3 jiao for food per day. Currently, about 100 baskets of coal are produced per day. The price of coal at the mine is 2 jiao per tan (240 jin) for powdered coal and 5 jiao per jin for lump coal. About 2,000 to 3,000 tan are sold each year. The mine tax is more than 30 yuan per year. The freight from the mine area to the Yellow River bank (ten li) is 2 jiao per carrying pole and 2.3 jiao per mule (each carrying pole about 200 jin). The tunnel uses natural ventilation, so mining has stopped because the wind is not circulating.

(3) Qiao'ergou Coal Mine: Located 5 li northwest of Shangyu Village and 65 li from the county seat. The coal is extracted from a vertical shaft, 4 feet in diameter and 130 feet deep. A horizontal adit is opened underground to the northeast for about 1,000 feet to mine coal. The ventilation shaft is more than 80 feet deep and uses natural ventilation. Each digger can dig 30 to 40 baskets of coal per shift. The wage is 300 copper coins. Each hauler can haul 30 to 40 baskets of coal (130 jin per basket) per shift. The wage is 300 copper coins. The eight windlass workers and one hooker above ground are paid 100 copper coins per shift. Food is provided by the workers themselves. There is very little lump coal. The price of raw coal is 1.5 jiao per tan. 30 to 40 tan can be sold per day. The wood used for support is about 4 inches in diameter and about 4 to 5 feet long. Each piece costs 1 jiao. Coal mining is temporarily suspended due to water. Bright lights are used underground, mostly burning rapeseed oil. The price of oil is 12 liang per yuan.

The geological age of Hancheng Coal Mine is Carboniferous Permian. The coal quality has been analyzed and the composition is fixed carbon 69.20 to 75.20, volatile matter 15.20 to 17.50, ash 6.80 to 9.60, sulfur 0.51 to 0.53, and calorific value 12000.

(4) Xigou Zhenyuan Coal Mine: Located 3 li west of Qiao'ergou. The Carboniferous coal system of Xigou is exposed on the side of the ditch, with more than 40 earth kilns. The current mine being mined is Zhenyuan Coal Mine, which is the largest in scale of all the mines examined this time. The mine owners are Li Xiaoguo and Yao Xinshan. The coal mine was bought in January of this year for 5,000 yuan. The coal pit is 200 feet deep and 4 feet in diameter. A horizontal adit is opened to the east and west from the bottom of the pit for 2,000 feet, and mining is carried out. The adit is 3 to 5 feet high and 2.5 to 4 feet wide. The coal seam is about 5 feet thick. The strike, dip, geology, coal quality, and ventilation are roughly the same as Qiao'ergou. Each digger digs 30 baskets per day. The wage is 300 copper coins. Each hauler hauls 40 baskets per day. The wage is 340 copper coins. Food and lamp oil are provided by the workers themselves. Currently, there are

Important News

three diggers, six haulers, one foreman, two windlass operators, three wheel pushers and one hooker (for a total of seventeen people) in the pit. The foreman's monthly salary is 20 yuan. The rest, except for the haulers, earn 300 copper coins per day (raw coal sells for 3 jiao per tan and the sales are very small. It is made into coke). The local area and Xi'an call it blue coal. It can be sold for 6 jiao per tan. The freight to Yumenkou (Yellow River bank), which is 15 li away, is about 4 jiao. Two jin of bituminous coal can make about one jin of coke. The coke oven is circular, 1 zhang in diameter and 7 feet deep. It can hold 40,000 jin of coal and produce about 20,000 jin of coke. The method is to fill the oven with 7 feet of coal and then build a wind tunnel on top with stones and cover it with coal ash. A fire door is opened on the lower side of the oven, and lump coal is used to start the fire. The fire is connected to all parts through the stone-built wind tunnel. Each oven can be burned for half a month. There are currently twelve or thirteen coke workers, each earning 5 yuan per month. However, those who build the stones earn 9 yuan per month. The water route from Yumenkou to Tongguan is 245 li, and the freight for every 100 degrees (24,000 jin) is about 112 yuan. The price of coke at Yumenkou is 130 yuan per 100 degrees. The water journey from Yumenkou to Baiyangzhai is about 334 li, and the freight for every 100 bundles is about 180 yuan. Each ship can carry dozens to four hundred bundles. The water depth of the Yellow River is usually about 2.5 feet, so the draft of the coal ship is at most 2 feet. Each large ship (carrying 400 bundles) costs about 800 to 900 yuan. Each ship employs about ten people. The land route from Baiyangzhai to Xi'an is about 110 li and is transported by livestock. The price of blue coal in Xi'an is usually around 3 yuan per 100 jin. The sandstone is very hard, so no support is needed. In addition, due to time constraints, the following were not examined: (1) Yushan Coal Mine: The coal quality is anthracite coal, which is mined by machine. The coal seam is about 24 feet thick and is located 110 li north of the county. (2) Ya Cha Coal Mine: The coal seam is about 6 feet thick and is located more than 80 li north of the city. (3) Qi Hu Chuan Iron Mine: Located more than 80 li north of the county. As for the water of Longmen, according to the surveyors, there is no electricity or anything else that can be used except for the passage of ships. However, the water of the Yellow River flowed to that place and was blocked by the big mountains, so the water had nowhere to go and flooded the fields, causing great harm. Yu then used divine skills to dig a mountain in half to allow the river water to flow. His great achievements are indeed an event that cannot be ignored for thousands of years.

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 70

▲Lawsuit Filed Regarding the Qingzhang Fee

The Ministry of Finance ordered this county to collect the Qingzhang fee starting this year, at a rate of one jiao per mu, and any fraction less than one jiao would be counted as one mu. This has caused various sectors to send telegrams appealing for the actual collection to be fair. As there are no instructions from the provincial government to Songjiang, organizations such as the Old Songjiang Charity Board, the chairman of Zhang Zhihe, the director of the asset management office, Li Zuhua, the executive committee member of the Food Management Committee, Ni Guangku, and the head of the First District, Shi Zhongtai, have jointly filed a lawsuit with the provincial government in accordance with Article 2, Paragraph 2 of the Law of Appeal, requesting that your esteemed government repeatedly

charge the Qingzhang fee, and there is no explicit provision that any fraction of a mu should be counted as one mu. The Ministry of Finance has even more severely and additionally collected fees, causing the people to bear non-obligatory donations. It is found that the land registration forms in Songjiang County have many fractions of hao and li. If fractions are rounded up, it is not fair in fact and violates the principle of tax rate in law. Historically, the collection of local surcharges has always been based on land tax, and there has never been a precedent for rounding up. If this malpractice is started, it will not only violate the order of your esteemed government's resolution, but also conflict with the prohibition of surcharges. Moreover, the people of Songjiang County have suffered repeated collections in recent years and have been affected by the war again. The people's livelihood has been extremely depressed, and it is unbearable to collect fees beyond the limit. The damage to the people's rights is not small. For this reason, a lawsuit is filed in accordance with the Law of Appeal, attaching a blank receipt from the Songjiang Financial Bureau, appealing to your esteemed government to order the Ministry of Finance to comply with the general plan and order the Songjiang County government to verify the collection in accordance with the land tax standard in order to relieve the people's difficulties and conform to the general plan, which is truly beneficial, etc.

Suzhou 71

▲ Suzhou Water Police Cooperate to Suppress Lake Bandits at Daquekou, Public Security Unit of the Water Police of Jiangsu Province, Third District, District Chief Shen Gaoli, based on reports that Henan, Anhui, Jiangbei, Pudong, Chaohu, and other bandits were gathering at Daquekou in the East Taihu Lake area to form a large-scale movement, specifically ordered the Fourteenth Team stationed in Wujiang, the Fifteenth Team in Pingwang, the Eighth Team in Dongshan, the Third Detachment of the Patrol Team in Ducun, and the Anjing and Zhenwei warships patrolling Taihu Lake to simultaneously depart on the third day to cooperate in the suppression. Also, bandits have been discovered near Yangchen Lake and Xiaogang at the junction of Suzhou, and District Chief Shen has ordered the Thirteenth Team to send troops to suppress them.

▲ The Case of a Fiancée Remaining Chaste Before Marriage Opens, Causing a Sensation in the City. The trial of the case of Xu Caizhen remaining chaste before marriage opened at 10:00 AM yesterday (the 3rd) at the Wuxian District Court. Xu Caizhen's father, Linshu, Xu Caizhen herself, the matchmaker Zhu Tianding, and lawyer Ma Heng were present. The defendant, Ma Yangshi, was absent due to illness. During the initial hearing, Xu Linshu and then Xu Caizhen were questioned. According to their testimony, Caizhen and Ma Baolin had been living together for six months. Although they were not married, they had essentially fulfilled the duties of husband and wife. Furthermore, Caizhen had stopped menstruating for three to four months, and it was possible that she was pregnant. They requested a judgment that Caizhen was a member of the Ma family, so as to fulfill her aspiration to remain chaste. The matchmaker, Zhu Tianding, testified that Caizhen and Baolin had indeed been living together for six months, and the groom's family had set the wedding date for December of this year. Finally, lawyer Ma stated and supplemented the facts. The court ordered that the case be adjourned for a retrial after summoning the defendant.

▲ Transfer of Weights and Measures Inspectors. Shen Benli and Tan Er, weights and measures inspectors of this county, were ordered to be transferred to Jiangyin and other places. Wang Zhenqing, a newly appointed first-class inspector, arrived in Suzhou on the 3rd to take over the work.

Taicang 72

▲ County Government Burns Opium and Leads to Disputes. On the first day of this month, the county government invited various agencies and organizations to gather at the large square in front of the county government to publicly burn opium, opium paraphernalia, and construction police supplies. More than 300 people from the public watched. At 1:00 PM, the items to be burned were submitted for inspection to the supervisors and representatives of the Party Headquarters item by item. Unexpectedly, when inspecting items numbered 12, 43, and 99, it was discovered that the packages contained yellow mud with no odor, and one number was missing. Immediately, the audience was greatly disturbed. Party Headquarters and organization representatives Zhu Qingzhao and others argued with County Magistrate Zhao Enju for a long time. Finally, the supervisors sealed the yellow mud and had the representatives sign the seal before submitting it to the High Court for resolution. No one raised any further objections regarding the remaining items, and they were publicly burned.

Wuxi 73

▲ Letter Requesting Restoration of Labor-Management Agreement. After the collapse of the silk factories in this county last year, tens of thousands of workers lost their jobs. It was hoped that work would resume with this year's spring harvest. However, harvests were poor in spring, summer, and autumn, and the silk market was sluggish. As a result, only about 20 silk factories in the county resumed operations, and some were only temporary. Due to the poor silk market, the wages of female silk factory workers could not be handled according to the previously agreed labor-management agreement. Therefore, the female workers requested the union to write to the employers to restore the agreement as soon as possible. The Organizing Committee of the Silk Factory Industry Union, Standing Committee members Xu Abao and Wang Dafu, based on the requests of the female workers, sent a letter to the Silk Factory Association yesterday (the 2nd) for their consideration and action.

▲ Late Indica Rice Appears on the Market. This year, both early and late rice crops have been damaged due to drought. Late indica rice has recently appeared on the market, and farmers are preparing to sow early wheat. However, due to the drought, the fields must be irrigated once before wheat can be planted. This year's late rice crop has a considerable amount of empty ears, especially the awned rice variety, which is particularly regrettable.

Changshu 74

▲ Robbery of Wheat Boat, Victim Injured. Lu Fu, a native of Wuxi, came to Changshu one day to buy wheat. The next day, while returning to Wuxi, he stopped for the night at Wangni Bridge on the border of Wuxi and Changshu. Unexpectedly, at around midnight, a boat with more than ten bandits suddenly arrived and robbed the wheat boat. Lu Fu resisted and was injured in the buttocks with a sectioned staff. A total of more than 400 yuan in cash and clothing were robbed. The victim reported the incident to the local public office the next morning, requesting an investigation.

Changzhou 75

▲ Bandits Alarmed Outside Dabeimen. The Northern Business Corps Patrol Team outside Dabeimen of Wu County, based on a tip-off on the evening of the 2nd, around 7:00 PM, that there were many bandits near Luowucun plotting a robbery, immediately dispatched Deputy Captain Zhang Youcai, carrying a pistol and in plain clothes, to investigate. Indeed, they saw five bandits. While questioning them, the bandits first opened a box gun to show off. Deputy Captain Zhang also returned fire, but he was outnumbered, and the pistol he was carrying was snatched away by the bandits. His head was also injured. At this time, Deputy Captain Zhang, still injured, fought with the bandits and stepped forward to capture the bandit who had snatched the gun, recovering the original gun. Fortunately, the police and corps in the city had already arrived. The remaining bandits, realizing the situation was not good, scattered and fled in the direction of the station. The captured bandit confessed his name as Mao Debiao and was handed over to the county government for interrogation on the 3rd.

After joint discussions, it was decided to implement temporary martial law to prevent accidents. Inspections are especially strict at all ports along the river and sea.

▲ Bandit Leader Feng Ziyun Has Been Escorted to the City. Feng Ziyun, a famous bandit leader north of the Yangtze River, was captured by the Joint Defense Guerrilla Team of Liuhe. He was transported to Tongcheng by gasoline boat, with strict precautions along the way. Bandit Feng confessed to the county government that he intended to rob Liuhe Town and then go to Haizhou after the crime.

They discussed 21 items related to defense and ordnance matters. The team leaders returned to their posts that night.

They were kidnapped and ransomed by the bandits after coming to Xinghua to run rice businesses. Inspector Liu escorted the kidnapped victims to Gaoyou last night (September 29th).

▲ Merchants and Residents Should Conduct Transactions According to the Price Conversion Table. The Zhenjiang County Weights and Measures Inspection Branch forwarded a request from the National Bureau of Weights and Measures, based on a report from the Hunan Construction Office, requesting instructions on how to punish merchants and residents who do not comply with the price conversion table for transactions. The Ministry of Industry issued Instruction No. 4980, stating that at the beginning of the implementation of the new system, acts of trading that do not comply with the price conversion table should be banned, and the provisions of Article 30, Paragraph 1 of the Remote Police Penalty Law should be applied, and the public security organs should impose penalties according to law when they are discovered, in order to warn against such behavior. This has been forwarded to the county, and the county inspection branch has recorded and notified each district to instruct merchants and residents to comply.

Education News

Special Article

Preliminary Ideas on Reforming Chinese School Education 80

(5) Cheng Tianfang

To supplement what is most important, the nation should quickly create more specialized primary education for the majority of the national population and productive elements. It is insufficient because many people did not have educational opportunities in the past and are now too old to attend primary school. Therefore, adult supplementary education should be used to make up for the deficiency in primary education. The length of study for such adult supplementary education institutions can be three months, half a year, or a year. They should also focus on both national knowledge and production skills. Since these two factors are not within the proper scope of this article, I will not elaborate.

The more primary schools that can truly cultivate healthy citizens and increase productive capacity, the better, because students from these primary schools will never become unemployed vagrants. Many of the current primary schools are private, and most are county-run. There are very few provincial schools, and there are absolutely no national schools. Many people believe that the state should focus on higher education, while primary education should be left to local or private organizations. I believe that while the state should focus on higher education, it should pay even more attention to primary education, because primary school is the foundation of education and the foundation of all politics and society. If primary schools are not run well, education will be poor, and politics and society will never improve. Especially in China, achieving the goal of universal national education cannot be accomplished by the financial resources of local or private organizations alone. Therefore, the state and provinces should allocate large sums of money to subsidize primary schools run by cities, counties, or private individuals. This funding should also be increased annually, with a deadline set so that national education is truly universal. Other agencies can be cut or merged, and government spending can be tightened, but this funding should absolutely not be saved or cut because this is the business to which China's future destiny is entrusted.

The intermediate education stage should include education for production, teachers, and the preparation of talent. Intermediate education is different from primary education. Primary education only has one type of school, namely primary school. Intermediate education can be divided into three types of schools with different characteristics: vocational schools, which focus on production education; normal schools, which focus on teacher education; and middle schools, which focus on preparing talent.

Chinese educators have advocated vocational education for more than a decade, and various provinces have established many vocational schools. But what is the effect? It can be said that most have failed. Since they are called vocational schools, their primary purpose is to enable graduates to produce and have proper occupations. However, the graduates of current vocational schools either go on to higher education if their families are well-off, or most join the ranks of the unemployed in society, searching for work all day long in a state of anxiety. A small number of those who have jobs are not at all related to the education they received in school. For example, graduates of industrial schools do not work in factories but become teachers in primary schools. Graduates of agricultural schools do not farm but work as clerks or secretaries in government offices. People who truly study a field and then work in that field are probably one in a hundred. Given this phenomenon, can it be said that past vocational schools were not a complete failure? We have studied the reasons for the failure of vocational schools. First, before the opening of each vocational school, the people in charge rarely have a precise plan for what kind of people society needs and what kind of people vocational schools should cultivate. They only follow their intuition in a general way. They feel that China's agriculture is not developing, so they open an agricultural school. They feel that China's industry is not developed, so they open an industrial school. As a result, the people created by the schools are not needed by society, and the people needed by society are not cultivated by the schools. Second, current vocational schools, like other schools, focus on book research and neglect practical skills. Students in agricultural schools sit in lecture halls listening to teachers talk about how to farm. Students in industrial schools sit in lecture halls listening to teachers talk about how to work. Even if students work very hard in such education, the result is the creation of waste. I have visited several vocational schools and personally seen that the rice seedlings transplanted by graduating students of agricultural schools are crooked and uneven, far inferior to those planted by uneducated farmers. The tools made by graduating students of industrial schools are rough and crude, far inferior to those made by uneducated workers. No matter how many such agricultural schools and industrial schools are run, they will naturally not affect China's agriculture and industry, and they will not be able to help students become productive elements. To correct these problems, I advocate that vocational schools should not be divided into departments such as agriculture, industry, and commerce. Instead, they should be divided into many different classes. They should open classes for the kind of people society needs, and they should not create people that society does not need. Second, vocational schools do not need to rigidly stipulate a graduation period of three, four, or five years. The length of study should be completely determined by the time required to train a certain production skill. Type A occupations may only require three months of training, and students can graduate in three months. Type B occupations may require half a year, Type C may require two years, and Type D may require five or six years. Even for the same occupation, if A wants to learn it well, it will take a year, while B only needs to learn a little and will only need half a year. Third, vocational schools should absolutely focus on skills training, with book teaching being secondary. Because the purpose of vocational schools is to create productive elements, not to cultivate specialized talents. What is most needed for ordinary production is practical skills, not principles. Therefore, it does not matter if students in vocational schools know less about principles. If they lack production skills, that is a fundamental loss of the meaning of vocational schools.
