Collision Between Qing Tian Warship and Jiang Yu Steamer 182

▲ Passengers and crew on the steamer unharmed

▲ One soldier injured on the warship

Recently, shipping accidents have occurred one after another. First, the Tonghua ran aground, then the Hua Wu was trapped in the fog and ran aground on the riverbank. Then the Xinfeng and Chao Wu collided, and the Zhoushan touched a reef in Yantai. Before one wave subsides, another rises. Now there is another collision between the China Merchants Bureau's Jiang Yu and the Hydrographic Office's Qing Tian warship. Yesterday afternoon, the Jiang Yu arrived in Shanghai. The details of the incident are recorded as follows:

▲Jiang Yu's Passage: The China Merchants Bureau's Jiang Yu steamer came to Shanghai from Hankou. At noon on October 1st, the ship arrived at Jiangyin. According to regulations, it stopped in front of the Jiangjing anchorage across the river to load and unload goods and passengers. At 10:23 PM that night, after the loading and unloading of goods and passengers was completed, the ship weighed anchor and set sail for Shanghai. It initially sailed at slow speed. At 10:30 PM, a dark shape was spotted on the starboard side of the ship. It was a ship without lights anchored on the river, obstructing the Jiang Yu's navigation. The captain, considering that it was difficult to identify the ship at night, ordered the helm to turn to the left to avoid the ship and ensure safe passage.

▲Two Ships Collide: When the Jiang Yu discovered a ship anchored on its starboard side, it quickly reversed course to the left. However, at that time, the tide was receding rapidly, and the bow of the Jiang Yu could not avoid the collision. The Jiang Yu's captain quickly stopped the ship and inspected it. He then realized that the ship at anchor was the Hydrographic Office's Qing Tian survey warship. But why did it not have stern lights on, leading to this collision? The Jiang Yu stopped, turned around, and sounded its whistle. It then lowered its anchor to rendezvous with the Qing Tian warship and jointly inspect the damage.

▲Extent of Damage: After the collision between the two ships, Jiang Yu's captain, Liu Hongce, visited Qing Tian and met with captain Chen Changqing. Together, they inspected and found that the steel plate on the left side of the bow of the Jiang Yu steamer, about ten feet wide and seven feet high, was damaged, and the iron plate on the bow anchor seat was also broken, and the iron chain was also broken. Fortunately, the breach was above the waterline, so the bow compartment was spared from flooding. The damage to the Qing Tian warship was the anchor hole in the bow was broken and the flagpole in the fore cabin was bent and broken. After both parties clarified the matter, they signed a joint certification.

▲Returning to Shanghai for Repairs: The Jiang Yu ship had no injuries to customers, but the Qing Tian warship had one petty officer, Chen Luyan, injured in the waist by the anchor chain during the collision and sent to the hospital for treatment. The Jiang Yu steamer did not set sail until 1:00 AM on the 2nd of the morning and arrived at Wusong yesterday morning at 10:35 and parked at the Jinliyuan wharf to unload cargo. In the afternoon, the captain reported to the bureau. The shipping department sent personnel to the ship to inspect and then repair the damage so that it could resume sailing.

▲The captain reported that after arriving in Shanghai, the captain reported the collision as it was. His ship, the sixth, arrived at Jiangyin on October 1st to stop loading and unloading cargo and passengers. The vessel started to navigate slowly at 10:23 PM and stopped after 26 minutes for a transfer from the left bank's vessel for transport. Unexpectedly, on the starboard side suddenly appeared a dark object like a sampan obstructing the navigation line. The vessel also did not have corresponding anchor lights lit. It was difficult to discern in the darkness what kind of vessel it was. The vessel could only steer to the right side as much as possible and was unable to reverse due to the extremely rapid ebb tide. The sharp maneuver led to the left bow of the vessel colliding with the other ship. Upon stopping to inspect, it was learned that it was the Qing Tian survey vessel. The issue of responsibility is still undecided.

Record of Hua Wu Steamer's Arrival in Shanghai After the Accident 183

The Nanhua Shipping Company's Hua Wu steamer ran aground near Zhenjiang, as reported previously. After several attempts, it was difficult to move the ship. The captain was left with no choice but to come to Shanghai to discuss rescue measures. He hired the most powerful tugboat from Wheelock Marden and set off for rescue the day before yesterday. However, the ship's hull was completely submerged, making the situation more dangerous than when the China Merchants Bureau's Tonghua ran aground at Huangshiqiu. In the former case, the ship was lightly loaded and small. In the latter, it was heavily loaded and large. The drag was long, but it was impossible to move the ship. Captain Yang Honglin, who had served as a pilot for many years and was experienced in water flow and sand lines, realized the danger. He devised a plan to move the ship's bow anchors and throw them into the river using iron barges, so that the ship's bow used the anchor's pulling force and the ship's stern used the tugboat's pulling force. The engines were simultaneously operated at full power, which successfully freed the ship. It was already aground for four days. Fortunately, the cargo loss was not severe. The ship arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon, and it is reported that the hull was not damaged.

Continued News on the Towing and Rescue of the Zhoushan Steamer 184

▲Unloading Cargo and Transporting to Weihaiwei: The Taikoo Company's Zhoushan steamer ran aground on a reef outside an island off the coast of Yantai. Because the bow compartment was flooded and trapped in the rocks, it was impossible to free the ship immediately. Therefore, Taikoo's Yantai branch dispatched a tugboat to the scene of the accident to unload a portion of the cargo from the Zhoushan steamer and transport it to the Weihaiwei wharf for storage in warehouses to reduce the weight of the Zhoushan steamer and make it easier to tow. Unloading is currently underway.

▲Japanese Ship Heading to Tow: A Japanese salvage company in Dalian has dispatched a tugboat to Yantai to prepare for the salvage operation. It is reported that the salvage plan is to use two large barges to support the Zhoushan steamer on the left and right, since only the bow compartment is flooded. This would raise it to the surface of the water, then repair the breaches, drain the accumulated water, and then tow it. This would be easier to accomplish. The British naval vessels HMS Kent and HMS Medway are still anchored alongside the Zhoushan to provide assistance.

▲Passengers Sent to Shanghai: All passengers on the Zhoushan ship have been rescued, including five Westerners and ninety-four Chinese, totaling ninety-nine people. After being rescued by a British naval launch to Yantai, the company has dispatched the Shuntian steamer from Tianjin to Yantai to transport these ninety-nine passengers to Shanghai. Yesterday afternoon, the Shanghai office received a telegram stating that the Shuntian steamer carrying the passengers is expected to arrive in Shanghai at 3:00 PM tomorrow afternoon.

Taxpayers' Association Held Executive Committee Meeting Yesterday 185

▲ Discussion on Water and Telephone Fees

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Shanghai Concession held its second executive committee meeting yesterday afternoon at 4 p.m. Those present included Zhang Yi, Wang Xiaolai, Pei Yunqing, Cheng Xiechun, Guo Shun, Dong Zhenlong, Xu Jiqing, Shen Tianxin, Yu Zhihao, Hu Fengxiang, Chen Jicheng, Xu Yongzuo, and Chu Seng Hua. Liu Hongsheng, Yuan Lvdeng, Bei Songsun, and others were also in attendance. Wang Xiaolai presided, Tao Leqin took minutes, and the meeting proceeded according to protocol. First, the chairman reported on the resolutions of the previous meeting, followed by a report on the association's affairs. Then, the following items were discussed: (A) Discussion on the English-owned Shanghai Waterworks Company's water fee calculation by meter, where the amount has increased sharply, affecting the livelihoods of ordinary citizens and small households. It was resolved to form an investigation committee to investigate the cost of water in the French Concession and Zhabei, as well as the installation methods of meters, the fee collection methods, and the reasons for the sharp increase in water fees. The candidates for the committee will be decided by the standing committee. (B) Discussion on the Shanghai Telephone Company's increase in usage fees and the retroactive collection of past fees. It was resolved that the price increase for telephone service and the retroactive collection of fees are absolutely unacceptable. (C) Discussion on the Shanghai Accountants Association's proposal that, as Chinese taxpayers within the concession contribute a large portion, Chinese professionals should participate in the review of the Shanghai Municipal Council's income and expenditure accounts. It was resolved that Mr. Hua should first make contact. (1) Regarding the Shanghai Municipal Council's method of waiving taxes north of the Suzhou Creek, there were no major disputes because of prior mutual consultation before the announcement. South of the Suzhou Creek, several companies sent letters requesting special consideration. The response was that the so-called special circumstances must be similar to the bombing of the Wing On Cotton Mill, and the matter was then resolved. (2) After the Shanghai Municipal Council's tax waiver measures north of the Suzhou Creek were announced, the association immediately sent a letter to the council stating that telephone and water fees should follow the same example. The council replied that it had discussed with the telephone and water companies and would handle them separately. However, many letters have been received requesting the association to negotiate due to the varying periods of free service. (3) A certain factory suspended operations, and a trade association sent a letter requesting the association to negotiate with the Shanghai Municipal Council for a tax waiver. The response was that the suspension of operations cannot be used as a reason for a tax waiver. (4) Disputes over the termination of lease agreements often occur when water is cut off. The response was that legal remedies should be sought. However, one clause in the Shanghai Municipal Council's contract states that if the property is still occupied, the water company must not cut off the water at the owner's request, and the owner is still responsible for the fees. It is unknown how the Shanghai Municipal Council interprets this. Attention should be paid to the fact that the contract provisions must be adhered to. (5) Regarding the matter of two Chinese members of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Land Committee, the consul general has consulted with the Shanghai Municipal Government according to Article 28 of the Yangjingbang Land Regulations and sought their consent on the method of selection. The Shanghai Municipal Government sent a letter to the association seeking its opinion for reference. The standing committee will invite committee members to discuss in detail and make a decision based on the principle of not violating the aforementioned regulations, and adopt a solemn approach. (6) Regarding the issue of telephone price increases, after receiving the news, the association immediately sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council explaining that the market was depressed after the Japanese disturbances in Shanghai, and there was no reason to increase prices. The council replied that the directors had taken note. Since then, the price increase has been implemented, starting in July of this year, with residential lines increasing from 52 taels of silver to 65 taels, and business lines from 78 taels to 105 taels. Each call increased from 5 cents in small silver coins to 4 cents in silver, and must be retroactive to March 27 of this year. Public opinion was in an uproar, with widespread opposition, especially to the retroactive nature, which was considered a violation of the legal principle of non-retroactivity. The Shanghai Evening Post attacked the increase vigorously, and the Shanghai Special District Telephone Users Association was also organized in response. The association repeatedly communicated the users' opinions to the Shanghai Municipal Council, and the director general replied that all documents were published in the gazette and there was no need to repeat them. However, regarding the retroactive nature, although the reasons were sufficient, citing contractual provisions, it was still unsatisfactory. Regarding the price increase after July, it would have been feasible without the Japanese disturbances in Shanghai. However, the Shanghai Municipal Council's telephone contract stipulated that automatic exchanges would also be installed in the outer road areas within two years. The Shanghai Municipal Government's obstruction allowed the company to be exempted from fulfilling its obligations. In fact, after the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities declared that the telephone company was responsible for the failure to install automatic exchanges, the basis for exempting the telephone company from fulfilling its contractual obligations was considered far-fetched. Even if the obstruction of automatic exchange installation was sufficient to exempt the telephone company from fulfilling its obligations, the users' inability to pay the increased price due to the Japanese disturbances was indeed an irresistible force. The Shanghai Municipal Council, as the executive body representing the taxpayers, insisted on enforcing contractual obligations, which was legally unpleasant, even though many paid under duress, and the issue remains unresolved. (7) The issue of water fee calculation by meter is significant. In the past, water fees were calculated based on rent, which had the effect of regulating wealth. To eliminate waste, meter calculation would prevent this effect from being lost, and it would be reasonable if all conditions were met. However, during a month when the atmosphere in Shanghai was extremely tense, the Shanghai Municipal Council signed a contract with the water company to adopt a meter system, and the basic price was not determined by a general meter installation cost experiment, but rather arbitrarily. As a result, the water fees calculated by meter were much higher than those calculated by rent, in some cases by as much as nine times, especially for poor small households. Water fees have traditionally been included in the rent paid by tenants, especially in poor small households, causing great panic among landlords. If they bear the cost themselves, they are unable to do so. According to Mr. Kui Yanfang, in one case, the rent was 100 yuan, but the water fee calculated by meter was 96 yuan. If added to the tenants' burden, it would increase the burden on the poor, contradicting Mr. Hill's opinion and fundamentally conflicting with the aforementioned principle of wealth regulation, making it extremely difficult to implement in practice. If this case is superficially viewed as only affecting landlords, it will eventually affect all users. If a reasonable and equitable solution is not urgently sought, the serious consequences are unimaginable. The crux of the matter is that the current director general, Mr. Jones, has too close a relationship with public utilities, resulting in a strong bias. Since entering the Shanghai Municipal Council, Mr. Jones has specialized in public utility cases, and many public utility contracts are his work. According to experts, these contracts are very favorable to companies and not favorable to taxpayers. For example, the long term of the water contract and the difficulty of changing or revoking it, as well as the restrictions on amending the bus contract requiring five years' notice, are all self-inflicted by the Shanghai Municipal Council and cannot be improved. Now that Mr. Jones is the director general, it is humanly impossible for him to not be prejudiced. This is why his only response to the association's repeated letters is to reiterate his published views.

Silk Workers' Strike Escalates in Severity: Resumption of Strike in the Concession Area Yesterday 188

▲ Disturbances Occur, One Female Worker Injured

▲ Male Workers in Silk Factories Across the City Also Make Demands

▲ Shuang Gong Silk Factory Fully Resumes Work Yesterday Morning

The labor-capital dispute at the single-reeling silk factories in this city has intensified. Yesterday afternoon, female workers in factories in the concession area resumed their strike, causing disturbances, with one person injured. The Yichang factory in Hongkou district is closing down. Female workers at the Shuang Gong factory resumed work yesterday. The details are as follows:

▲ Strike Resumes in the Concession Area: At 1 p.m. yesterday, female workers at the Xiangfeng Silk Factory on Gansu Road in the concession area suddenly went on strike. The situation became chaotic as all workers left the factory and gathered at the Jingwei Factory on Arbuthnot Road, demanding that they join the strike. The factory authorities, seeing the fierce momentum, were unable to dissuade them, and the working female workers were panicked and had no choice but to stop the machines and release the female workers. As a result, many female workers gathered at the Longyuan, Runchang, and Xuxiang factories on the same road. By around 2 p.m., all five factories, including Xiangfeng, had fully joined the strike. During the strike, the Huishan Police Station of the Public Concession received a report and dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to stop it, resulting in a conflict with the female workers. A female worker named A Mao from the Xiangfeng factory workshop was injured and fell to the ground. She was taken back to her home by the other female workers for treatment.

▲ Trade Union States Reasons: A reporter from New Voice News Agency interviewed the director of the Third District Silk Reeling Trade Union yesterday to discuss the reasons for the resumption of the strike: (1) It has been many days since they accepted the advice to resume work, but no effective solution has been seen. (2) The factories will be paying wages on the 5th and claim that they will still be paying 4.5 jiao, with no increase at all. (3) The factory authorities announced that the female workers in the district have no hope of increasing their wages and that it is the mischief of a few. The trade union planned to send personnel to persuade them, but because the personnel were accused of coercing the strike during the last strike, it was not convenient to send personnel this time to avoid being falsely accused. They only hope that the party and government organs will promptly and impartially handle the matter.

▲ Workers Also Make Demands: After the labor-capital dispute at the silk factories, the male workers at the silk factories that have started work across the city also gathered to request that the trade union propose: (1) Restore the silkworm chrysalis price to 4.5 jiao per yuan. (2) Restore the four working days per month. The Third and Fourth District Silk Reeling Trade Unions separately submitted requests to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters yesterday to mediate.

▲ Trade Union Petitions Yesterday: In view of the extension of the female workers' strike, each silk factory in Hongkou plans to close down. Yesterday, the Yichang Silk Factory closed down and issued the female workers their savings. The Fourth District Silk Reeling Trade Union sent staff member Lu Xusheng to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday to request that they be stopped and to promptly find a way to mediate the labor-capital dispute at the silk factories. Director Wang Xianqing of the Mediation Section received them and promised to discuss the matter with the Party Headquarters and the Public Security Bureau. At 3 p.m., the Third District Silk Reeling Trade Union sent staff member He Yin to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau to report on the resumption of the strike by workers in the concession area, requesting impartial mediation, which was fully accepted.

▲ Shuang Gong Resumes Work Yesterday: After a misunderstanding between male and female workers at the Fulun Shuang Gong Silk Factory on Tianhe Road in Hongkou, the factory manager and the government provided detailed explanations and obtained the female workers' understanding. Work resumed at the factory yesterday morning. At the same time, the Fifth District, Third Sub-station of the Municipal Public Security Bureau sent police to protect the factory, and by 6 a.m., all the workers had entered the factory to resume work in good order.

Shanghai South Bus Workers' Strike: Mediation by the Social Affairs Bureau Yesterday Proves Ineffective 190

▲ Labor Refuses to Vacate Factory Premises

According to Da Gong She, the dispute over the suspension of business by the Shanghai South Bus Company was mediated by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, which convened both parties at 2 p.m. yesterday. Labor representatives Qian Shunlin, Hu Jinshan, and Qiao Jihe, employer representatives Xu Jiqin and Chen Gongcheng, and Municipal Party Headquarters representative Fan Guoren were present. Peng Zhenqiu of the Social Affairs Bureau presided and Wang Zhiqin took minutes. The chairman first explained that the case has yielded no results after two interrogations and that the employer failed to attend the third meeting. However, due to the workers' dire financial straits, they have repeatedly presented requests for mediation. Therefore, the bureau convened formal mediation, hoping that both labor and management would seek a resolution to the case in a more favorable manner. Employer representative Xu Jiqin then stated that the company had previously paid off the workers' back wages under the supervision of representatives from the party and government organs, and the workers had agreed to leave the factory. Now the labor side has violated the intentions of the party and government and, on the 28th of last month, still used the excuse to enter the factory and seize vehicles, which is hindering the accountant's liquidation work. The bureau should immediately notify them to withdraw and that the company believes that the case has come to an end in terms of the dispute and that there is no need for further mediation. Labor representative Qian Shunlin then stated that the workers' entry into the factory this time was not illegal because the accountant Jiang Wanping, entrusted by the company, stated when paying the back wages that the liquidation period would be about two weeks and that it would be reported to the party and government organs for review. Since the suspension of business, it has been over a month, and there is still no indication of when the accountant's liquidation will be completed. The workers are compelled by their financial situation and have no choice but to enter the factory, but they have not seized any vehicles and are not hindering the accountant's liquidation. They cannot accept the company's representative's request for the workers to withdraw from the company before the dispute is resolved. The dispute on the spot was very tense. The chairman then held individual talks, but the labor and management each held their own ground and the proposed solutions were not close. The employer representatives were instructed to consult with the shareholders and provide a definitive solution. A reply will be provided this morning. The labor representatives were also notified to submit a list of the wages of each worker for several months to the bureau for further handling.

Chamber of Commerce Writes to the Finance and Health Bureaus Requesting Postponement of Salted Pork Inspection 191

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent separate letters to the Finance and Health Bureaus, stating that on September 30, the Salted and Preserved Meat Trade Association sent a letter stating that (omitted)... This case has been opposed by the salted and preserved meat and ham industries since the bureau proposed it. Because the reasons were not listed, they were not conveyed. The current statement is that the salted pork is transported from other ports and repeatedly salted. Although the appearance is dirty, the quality is definitely not rotten. It has been sold in Shanghai for a long time, and those who like it have not had any adverse reactions. There is no need to inspect it. Since 1928, the city's commerce has been in a slump, and salted pork is no exception. Now that the goods and sales are both weak, it will be even more difficult to maintain business if inspection fees are added. This is the second reason why it should not be inspected. The situation is not without considerable reason. We are sending this letter to your bureau with the request that you review and temporarily postpone the implementation of this measure to alleviate the difficulties of the merchants.

Shanghai County Political Meeting Record 192

121st Meeting

The Shanghai County Government held its 121st County Political Meeting at 10 a.m. yesterday. The heads of the finance, construction, and education bureaus, the director of the Treasury, the secretary of the County Government, and section chiefs attended. County Magistrate Yan Shenyu chaired the meeting and Hu Gongshou took minutes. The following cases were discussed and resolved: (1) The county magistrate submitted for discussion a report from the Finance Bureau stating that it had been ordered to allocate 300 yuan of silver from the local funds to repay Jiang Ren for the advance payment of the public expenses for borrowing boats to manage debt collection from debtors, and asked how the county should handle the matter. It was resolved that the local finances were extremely difficult, the annual budget had already been determined, and there were indeed no funds available to allocate. It was requested that the Finance Department approve the allocation from the collection of old debts and provincial taxes. (2) The county magistrate submitted for discussion a request from the County Construction Bureau for the First District Office to request a reduction in the ferry license fee and asked how the county should handle the matter. It was resolved that, at the beginning of operation, a fee of 1.5 yuan would be temporarily permitted to be collected.

Huang Naishu Resigns as Director of the Postal Bureau 193

Director Huang Naishu of the Postal Bureau has submitted his resignation to the Ministry of Transportation because the bureau's income has been greatly reduced since the Northeast postal service was blocked, making it impossible to maintain operations. The Ministry of Transportation believes that Huang has made outstanding achievements and has been deeply reliant on him, so he ordered him to be retained and sent Postal Director Lin Shi to Shanghai to personally comfort and retain him. It is now heard that Huang's intention to resign is still very firm and he has telegraphed the ministry to request his resignation. He intends to handle the handover as soon as it is approved.

Page 17

Liang Zuoyou Donates Money to Save the Country 194

Liang Zuoyou, a righteous man from Shandong, donated 30 million yuan to relieve the national crisis. The first telegram was sent, and I doubted its accuracy, because in our economically backward country, I had never heard of a Shandong businessman with assets exceeding 70 or 80 million. I suspected that the word "thousand" or "ten" was a mistake. Unexpectedly, subsequent telegrams confirmed it. Therefore, I have not given up on the inheritance system. The idea of rights is developing in our country, and Liang Zuoyou can donate generously. The fact that he is admirable is beyond words, and I don't need to repeat it.

According to Liang Zuoyou, the expenditure of the economic funds is divided into three categories: 20% to subsidize bandit suppression funds, 20% to relieve unemployed disaster victims, and 60% to revitalize industry. In terms of the quantity and nature of the expenditure, it meets the essential standards for alleviating the national crisis.

However, our country's economy has never been transparent. The people have no idea about the country's income, expenditure, and their uses. It is inevitable that funds will be used for different purposes than originally intended. As long as there is money, it will be used first, and then we'll talk about it. Our country's economy is in such a chaotic state and has become a habit. I don't know if the government can follow Liang Zuoyou's intention in spending the economic funds, or if it will make people doubt. Some say that Liang Zuoyou's donation should be used to set up a custody committee to oversee the use. However, this system is not applicable in our country. For example, the Palace Museum also has a custody committee, but the result is still that there are cases of stealing and selling palace artifacts. The establishment of a custody committee is meaningless.

Liang Zuoyou donated 30 million yuan, and his purpose of relief is such. But Liang Zuoyou has already donated, so the government will properly spend the economic funds. Liang Zuoyou is just doing what he feels is right, and there is no need to worry about the aftermath.

The wind and clouds in Shandong Province have not yet cleared, and the poor people in several counties are fish on the chopping board. The internal strife has not yet stopped. Who broke our good home?

The sound of singing and music is clear in the night air of the building, and the bright moon shines on the foreign land for ten miles. The past events of enduring hardship and tasting bitterness are now used to decorate the prosperity and enjoy peace.

Half of the Chinese rivers and mountains have been lost, and the traitors endure humiliation and call themselves subjects. People are sleeping next to our beds. I am ashamed of the Liaoning Volunteer Army.

We rely on the League of Nations for peace for a year, but the news of peace is still vague. We must not abandon the lessons of the past. The鹬蚌相爭鹬蚌相争 (鹬蚌相争: idiom meaning when two parties fight, a third party benefits) must be quelled first.

Science

Talking About Several Kinds of Bottle Sealing Products Shen Min 196

Whether it is Western medicine, chemical reagents, industrial chemicals, or cosmetics, flavors, etc., such as things that are volatile or absorbent. Although they have been stored in bottles, they have been sealed with glass stoppers or corks. But it's still not suitable. You must add a kind of solid sealing object. There are many kinds of these items. Use compatible items to seal according to their different natures and prices. For example, for things that are absorbent. Common items can be used for sealing. If it is a volatile or combustible substance. You have to be careful. Because ordinary solid sealants. Such as sealing wax, Faraffn, etc. have to be melted with fire. Carelessness can be dangerous. Although the sealing object is very small. But its use is also very wide. Now I will talk about them separately.

Ordinary Solid Sealants

These solid sealants are mostly used for absorbent items. Such as mineral salts. As well as cheap and non-combustible items, etc. Its main products. Such as sealing wax, is a rosin compound. Faraffn is a mineral wax extracted from kerosene, etc. It can be melted into a liquid with fire first. Then pour it on the bottle mouth. Everyone probably knows about these very common things. No need to say more.

Special Solid Sealants

This sealing object is used on bottle mouths that store volatile or combustible substances. Also expensive medicines. Or commercial products that need to look beautiful. This type of sealing object must also be used. There are many kinds of it. They all need to be manufactured. They are not naturally generated. So they need to be explained separately as follows. But limited by space. I can only cite two kinds.

(1) Guncotton Sealing Object Its raw material is Eollodion. The method of making Eollodion is to dissolve Tolubbpyroxylin in Etoet. It becomes a thick solution. The bottle mouth is coated with this liquid substance. It can solidify into a transparent thin layer in a few minutes. It adheres to the bottle mouth. If you want to be beautiful. You can use various pigments. Add it to the Eollodion liquid in advance. The bottle mouths of various cosmetic fragrances on the market. More expensive ones have this kind of solid sealing object wrapped around the bottle mouth. Its advantage is that it does not need to be melted with fire, so there is no danger of combustion.

(2) Glycerin Compound Sealing Object Glycerin is an oily substance. Is it also good to use for sealing objects? Isn't that strange? But chemistry is a matter of endless changes. Readers, please don't be impatient. Wait for the author to tell you the principle and method of making it. Add fine powder of Okiadeoflrad (commonly known as litharge) to thick glycerin. These two items, one dry and one wet. Mix them together. It can be turned into a very strong Eement. Because litharge is a substance with extremely high drying properties. So glycerin, although it is a non-drying substance. If you use too much litharge. It will also dry and solidify. Its use. It is best used on the mouths of bottles of petroleum, gasoline, Eollodion, basin pure, de-wood spirits, etc. Because it has no danger of catching fire.

Improvement Society Discussion Meeting

On the Need for Improvement of Popular Reading Materials by Zeng Yu 197

In Chinese society, where education is so underdeveloped, the need for and improvement of popular reading materials is truly urgent. This is because the general population who have not received education naturally know very few characters. For their reading materials, it is essential that the meaning is simple and the characters clear. Although there is now a profusion of novels on the market, finding one suitable for the common people can be said to be rarer than hen's teeth. In the past, one often saw rickshaw pullers like Little Sanzi and apprentices at blacksmith shops like Afu, and vegetable sellers like Wang Si, reading books while cooling off in the streets and alleys. However, if you were to look at the titles of their books, they would invariably be something like "Meng Jiangnu," "Four Seasons Mountain Songs," or "Suzhou Scenery, Eighteen Touches," etc. These kinds of meaningless little books can almost be considered

Page 18

their only reading material. Given this situation, their knowledge only gets worse. There are also those who know a little more characters and are keen on reading novels of the kind that are "China's Only Family Treasure for Thousands of Years"—supernatural and superstitious stories with flying swords, heroic knights-errant, immortals, and demons fighting each other (these kinds of books are still emerging endlessly in bookstores). This is even more harmful, and simple-minded people, poisoned by them, often daydream about becoming sword immortals (last year, a newspaper reported that an apprentice at a shop in Wuxi ran away, leaving a letter saying that he was going to Mount Emei in Sichuan to learn Taoism). In this time of national crisis, some people even say, "The Japanese are not to be feared; our Chinese sword immortals and knights-errant are about to be born!" These kinds of people are obsessed with absurd novels, and their intelligence is obliterated. How pitiable this is! However, the harm of these novels is not limited to this; I will only briefly mention one or two points.

Regarding the improvement of this problem, first, all bookstores in the market should stop printing all kinds of absurd novels from now on, and all unsold copies must be sealed and hidden. Second, those who write novels in the future must change their purpose. The content of the novels must be suitable for the times, or have scientific (simple) interest, relevance to the current situation (such as national crisis), or contain common sense, art, etc. In short, they must no longer write supernatural, superstitious, or obscene absurd novels. Third, it is best to have each novel reviewed before it is published. Fourth, more public libraries for the common people must be established in various places (because there are very few reading materials suitable for the common people in existing libraries). These libraries should specifically select the most common and meaningful reading materials for the common people, and have scholars on hand to provide guidance at any time so that the common people in society have books to read in their leisure time. In that case, their level of knowledge can at least be increased a little, and they will not engage in various useless pastimes in their spare time.

A Corner of Society

The Female Writer in the Park by Wu 198

A truly intelligent female writer, she actually sensed the intensity of the autumn. When she came to this park alone, it was exceptionally refreshing. "Ah, how refreshing it is! The red leaves are embracing me, the cool breeze is caressing me. Ah! How beautiful it is! Oh, this autumn, this poetry-filled autumn!"

At this moment, our female writer was greatly inspired because she truly touched things that ordinary, uninspired people could not feel. So we saw her take out the draft of her creations, as if it were her life, from her glossy handbag, and create with her gold-plated fountain pen with a rustling sound. It is most regrettable that this is, after all,

an empty wilderness. The beautiful sound of writing is not as crisp as it would be in a delicate study. However, her heart was filled with unrestrainable emotion, which, of course, is something that we uninspired people would not feel.

She continued to write, she kept writing: "...Oh! This urban serenity, this great gift of nature."

Pairs of affectionate men and women passed before her, and every young man looked at her with affection. This made her feel honored and also made a flash of envy surge in her heart. So she put down her pen, took out the pocket mirror that she carried with her from her handbag, and reapplied makeup to her face. Her hair was so fluffy, and her cheeks were so delicate and charming. So she felt satisfied, satisfied, especially since she was already a famous writer. So she could not help but smile derisively at those artificially made-up beautiful young women:

"You soulless daughters, you don't need to boast to me about your husbands in their prime. If your husband is a lover of literature and art, if your husband knows that I am a famous writer and has read my works, wouldn't he abandon you and throw himself into my arms?"

In this way, she felt victorious.

Then she heard men whispering beside her:

"I think she must be a female novelist. Look at her writing non-stop. Otherwise, an ordinary woman would not write in the park."

"No, I don't think so," said another. "She must be writing a love letter. She can't be a great female writer because we know that every great artist is unkempt and likes natural beauty. But she looks like she came from a beauty salon. She is completely dressed like a concubine and has no literary flair at all."

This was enough to make her angry. "Are there no exceptions among literary figures? Can't I decorate myself if I have money?"

However, this was the criticism of young men. Men's vision is such, and female literary figures should be like this and that. In the end, she cannot go beyond the scope of an artist, so it is not convenient to have a special stereotype.

So our novelist had a new understanding. She might as well temporarily put away the beautiful inspiration she had gained in the autumn and hurried out of the park.

In the rickshaw, her mood was so anxious. She decided to immediately go back to straighten her hair and wash off her makeup. But the thin rickshaw puller was running so slowly, apparently deliberately making things difficult for her. So she scolded loudly:

"You lazy fellow, don't you have legs? Why can't you run like this?"

This was naturally justified to her: she had the money, and she had hired this rickshaw puller. Of course, she could scold him, and it would be okay to hit him a few times.

She, such a writer. That's all, that's all.

Hearsay

The Magical Photography by Zhao Shukui 199

Any school or institution that recruits or holds examinations requires a four-inch photograph in addition to certificates and diplomas. With a photograph, it is possible to verify whether the person and the photo match and to prevent the abuse of substitutions. This is indeed a good method.

However, yesterday I met a friend who runs a photography studio and said: Photography studios now have a newly invented mixed photography, which is a good thing to make it easier for students to apply for exams. For example, if A wants to apply to a certain school but his level is too poor, he has to find B to take his place. However, the faces in the photos are different. As long as B is scheduled to go to the photography studio with A in advance to take the photo, A will be photographed first, and then B will be photographed. If A is strong and B is thin, B might as well wear more clothes and wear them so that they look as bulky as A. If A's eyes are big and B's eyes are small, A might as well narrow his eyes, and B might as well widen his eyes. The photo taken will be eight parts like B and two parts like A. After a few weeks, B has completely faded away and becomes a very clear A. This kind of mixed photography is very expensive and costs four or five yuan per photo! Haha! Such photography is really a new invention of the 21st century!

Casual Chat

Bumping into the Rice Basket by Jingxiang 200

In a certain section of a certain concession, there are those people selling food and opium to those blacklisted people who have lost face, bent their backs, and shrugged their shoulders. The food stores are surrounded by many idlers and ruffians who specialize in blackmail, intimidation, and pickpocketing. Those who come to buy food naturally suffer endlessly! It's just that they themselves are also guilty of private lawlessness. If they are blackmailed, they can only recognize their bad luck, just like a "mute eating coptis chinensis," they can't speak of the bitterness. It is better not to speak of it, and even if you want to say something, you don't dare to. Therefore, these ruffians and idlers can enjoy themselves in it, happy to do it, and it is not only helping to fuel their arrogance, but also leading to unbridled rampage! The sins are intertwined. There are countless servants!

I have a friend who often likes to joke. Once, he had some fun with that kind of idler. The story is very funny. He told me this: One night, my friend pretended to be wandering around these food stores in the French Concession, looking around idly. Before he knew it, he heard urgent footsteps behind him. I turned around and saw a man in a blue cloth short coat. I thought this must be a lookout of some kind of idler. He probably thought that I was here to buy black rice, so I simply used his plan and joked with him. Once I made up my mind, I pretended to be timid and at the same time picked up my two legs and ran forward quickly. When he saw me running fast, he followed closely. As a result, he opened his mouth to shout at me first.

"Hey! Friend, run slower, be sensible." While

saying this, he quickened his pace and came straight to my side. I took the opportunity to give him a clear greeting and saw

Page 19

that his peaked cap was crookedly on his head, and his two eyes were slippery and scary. Fortunately, there was only one person, so I might as well play with him. So I said to him:

"Oh! Old friend, we are all family, so it's fine." "How much are you buying? Let's take care of each other." He said.

"I'm not buying much, just a little, but old friend, I'm unlucky. The money I had just ran out, so I have to ask you to walk a few more steps and come with me to my house to get it, okay?" I said to him.

"Where is your house?" He asked impatiently.

"It's just a little way, it's just ahead." I lied to him again.

So he just followed me, and I circled around east and west. After walking for a while, he always impatiently urged, "Have we arrived yet?" I always said to him, "Soon, soon." Walking, walking, I had already passed Avenue Edward VII. According to the rules of their idlers, there are separate sections. I thought he would be sensible and wouldn't follow, but who knew he wouldn't let go and still clung to me. I looked forward and saw that I was almost at Avenue des Deux Republiques. The red wall of the police station was already visible. So I came up with an idea and turned my head to look back at him and said:

"This time, we are really arriving at my house, it's just ahead." While pointing to the police station to show him. When he saw it, he immediately panicked.

"F***!" He didn't even finish cursing, his two eyes wide open, and he hurriedly turned around and ran away. I couldn't help but clap my hands and laugh. He had been fooled. Thinking about it now, I still find it endlessly interesting!

▲Civil First Instance Judgment: Chan Baiyang, Li Deki versus Dasen Factory, et al., for Order Case (Ruling): Defendant Dasen Factory should repay the plaintiff silver 8,167 taels, 0 yuan, 4 mace, and 7 fen. Both should also repay interest at a rate of 7% per annum from September 1st until the date of completion of execution, as well as warehouse rent, insurance fees, and taxes. Simultaneously, each should also extract the ordered cotton yarn, 25 pieces, from the plaintiff. Defendant Zhu Fuhua is responsible for clearing and repaying the above-mentioned portion. The plaintiff's request for provisional execution is rejected. The litigation costs will be borne by the defendant Dasen Factory and Dasheng Factory in proportion.

Good Coming versus Yuanshun Xieji, et al., for Goods Payment Case (Ruling): Defendant Yuanshun Xieji and Lezhengji should pay the plaintiff silver 2,070 taels. If unable to pay, Defendant Jiuchang Rice Store is responsible for paying on their behalf. Defendant Li Lianji should pay the plaintiff 2,070 taels. If unable to pay, Defendant Liu Fengxiang is responsible for paying on their behalf. Defendant Cuixin Xieji and Chen Longsheng should pay the plaintiff silver 2,030 taels. If unable to pay, Defendant Qinyi Xieji Store Owner is responsible for paying on their behalf. Defendant Yang Hanji should pay the plaintiff silver 1,650 taels. If unable to pay, Defendant Dete Company Store Owner is responsible for paying on their behalf. Defendant Wang Qiming should pay the plaintiff silver 1,670 taels. If unable to pay, Defendant Jiecheng Company Store Owner is responsible for paying on their behalf. Defendant Zou Chengji should pay the plaintiff silver 2,250 taels. If unable to pay, Defendant Jiang Hengxing Store Owner is responsible for paying on their behalf. The plaintiff's remaining claims are rejected. The litigation costs are borne by the plaintiff for 60% of the total. The remaining costs are borne by the defendant Lezhengji, Li Lianji, Chen Longsheng, Yang Hanji, Wang Qiming, and Zou Chengji in proportion. This judgment declares provisional execution.

Yushengli Heji Leather Store versus Renji Company, et al., for Goods Payment Case (Ruling): Defendant Renji Company should repay the plaintiff for goods 12.634 yuan in foreign currency. Defendant Zhongnan Factory should repay the plaintiff for goods 25.49 yuan in foreign currency. Defendant Ling Jujin should repay the plaintiff for goods 185.645 yuan in foreign currency. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant Renji Company for 1/10, the defendant Zhongnan Factory for 2/10, and the defendant Ling Jujin for 4/10. The remaining costs are borne by the plaintiff.

▲White Ta Ge versus Yuan Kui Sheng for Debt Case (Ruling): The plaintiff's claim is rejected. The litigation costs are borne by the plaintiff.

▲Aierde Company, Landlord Chen Jisheng versus Lvyang Photo Studio for Rent Arrears, et al. (Ruling): The defendant should repay the plaintiff 750 yuan and return the premises to the plaintiff. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲Public Works Bureau versus China Iron Factory for Donation Arrears Case (Ruling): The defendant should repay the plaintiff donation arrears of silver 105 taels. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲Song Hongsheng versus Shen Abing et al. for Debt Case (Ruling): Defendants Shen Abing and Chen Lian should jointly and severally repay the plaintiff debt of 40 yuan in foreign currency, with interest calculated at an annual rate of 20% from June 6, 1926, until the date of full payment. The plaintiff's remaining claims are rejected. The litigation costs are jointly and severally borne by the defendants Shen Abing and Chen Liansheng.

▲Taili Company versus Zhan Songsan for Rent Arrears Case (Ruling): The defendant should repay the plaintiff rent of 252 yuan in foreign currency and street cleaning fee of 32 jiao in small foreign currency. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲Hu Yuanxiang versus Hanli Company et al. for Debt Arrears Case (Ruling): Defendant Xiangkang Hardware Store should repay the plaintiff 32 yuan in foreign currency and 40 taels and 4 qian in silver. Defendant Hanli Company should repay the plaintiff 220.52 yuan in foreign currency. The litigation costs are borne by the defendants proportionally according to the amount of their claim.

▲Tan Shisheng versus Xue Liansheng et al. for Debt Case (Ruling): Defendant Xue Liansheng should repay the plaintiff debt of 260 yuan in foreign currency, to be repaid in equal installments over 20 months from the date of judgment. The remaining claims are rejected. The litigation costs, except for the part concerning Jiang Zhifu which is borne by the plaintiff, are borne by the defendant Xue Liansheng.

▲Jiang Laixing versus Wang A'da et al. for Debt Case (Ruling): Defendants Wang A'da and Wang Chunji should each repay the plaintiff debt of 150 yuan in foreign currency, to be repaid in equal installments over 10 months from the date of judgment. The remaining claims are rejected. The litigation costs are borne equally by the defendants Wang A'da and Wang Chunji.

▲Qianye Guild Hall, Landlord Accounting Office versus Zhang Zhichun for Rent Arrears Case (Ruling): The defendant should repay the plaintiff rent of 128 yuan. The lease agreement between both parties is permitted to be terminated. The defendant should vacate the premises and return them to the plaintiff. Provisional execution is not permitted for the part concerning vacating the premises. The remaining claims are rejected. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲Tongming Gas and Electric Company versus Xibiliya Fur Store for Rent Arrears Case (Ruling): The defendant should pay the plaintiff

rent of 81 taels and removal fee of 5 taels. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

Xu Yaozhang versus Lu Genlan for Goods Payment Case (Ruling): The defendant should repay the plaintiff for goods 290.66 yuan. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲Song Hongsheng versus Si Hualun et al. for Debt Case (Ruling): Defendant Si Hualun should repay the plaintiff debt of 600 yuan in foreign currency, with interest calculated at 1.5% per month from February 15, 1932, until the date of full payment, to be repaid in equal installments over 10 months from the date of judgment. If his assets are insufficient to repay the aforementioned debt, Defendant Qian Yi Ke Fu is responsible for repaying 400 yuan in foreign currency on his behalf. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant Si Hualun for 5/6 and by the defendant Qian Yi Ke Fu for 1/6.

▲Xie Yibin versus Cai Hongguang for Debt Arrears Case (Ruling): The defendant should repay the plaintiff 874 yuan and 7 li, and interest at 1% per month from May 19, 1928, until the date of completion of execution. The plaintiff's remaining claims are rejected. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant for 4/5 and by the plaintiff for 1/5.

▲A'qin Taili versus A'qin Taili Si, Partnership Liquidation Appeal against Execution Case (Ruling): The application is rejected. The application costs are borne by the applicant. (Above, October 3rd)

Shanghai Second Special District Local Court 203

▲Criminal Judgment: Police Department versus Huang Quangen et al. for Opium Case (Ruling): Huang Quan is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for the crime of providing premises for others to smoke opium substitutes with the intention of profit. Bu Wenxue is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for the crime of smoking opium substitutes, a repeated offense. Wang Pengnan and Zhang Bingtou are each sentenced to one month of imprisonment for the crime of smoking opium substitutes. The number of days in custody before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days for each person. Xu Wangshi is innocent. Wang Pengnan and Zhang Bingtou are each given a two-year suspended sentence. Nine opium pipes are confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department versus Chen Jiafa et al. for Intimidation Case (Ruling): Chen Jiafa and Wang Baoyao are each sentenced to imprisonment for the crime of joint intimidation. The number of days in custody before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days for each person.

▲Police Department versus Luo Jinbao for Theft Case (Ruling): Luo Jinbao is sentenced to nine months of imprisonment for theft as a profession. The number of days in custody before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days. Qian Zao's Bing is confiscated.

▲Police Department versus Cai Jin Shi et al. for Professional Theft and Stolen Goods Case (Ruling): Cai Jin Shi is sentenced to three years and six months of imprisonment for theft as a profession. A Liang is sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment for theft as a profession, a repeated offense. Chen Ahua is sentenced to four months of imprisonment for dealing in stolen goods as a pawnbroker. The number of days in custody before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days for each person.

▲Police Department versus Zhang Fengming et al. for Intimidation and Opium Case (Ruling): Zhang Fengming is sentenced to four months of imprisonment for the crime of joint intimidation and six months of imprisonment for the crime of providing premises for others to smoke opium substitutes. The total imprisonment is eight months. Ye Yukang is sentenced to three months of imprisonment for assisting in providing premises for others to smoke opium substitutes.

Miao Fengchun is sentenced to one month of imprisonment for the crime of smoking opium substitutes. The number of days in custody before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days for each person. Miao Fengchun is given a two-year suspended sentence. Opium pipes, "Hong Wan" pills, silver shavings, and other items are all confiscated.

▲Police Department versus Wang Ziming et al. for Robbery and Stolen Goods Case (Ruling): Wang Ziming, Fei Yongxing, Yu You, and Jiang Yihai are each sentenced to five years of imprisonment for the crime of carrying weapons and committing joint robbery with three or more people. Qian Jue is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for the crime of receiving stolen goods. The number of days in custody before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days for each person. Two handguns and seven bullets are confiscated.

▲Police Department versus Dai Hanbin et al. for Suspected Robbery Case (Ruling): Dai Hanbin is sentenced to eight months of imprisonment for the crime of possessing a military handgun and bullets with the intent to commit a crime. The number of days in custody before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days. One handgun, fifteen bullets, and two cartridge boxes are confiscated. Li Hairu is innocent.

▲Police Department versus Wang Zhou Shi et al. for Opium Case (Ruling): Wang Zhou Shi is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for the crime of providing premises for others to smoke opium substitutes with the intention of profit. Zhang Deji, Wu Zhiquan, He Bingquan, and Shen Dequan are each sentenced to one month of imprisonment for the crime of smoking opium substitutes. Li Jinrong is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for the crime of smoking opium substitutes, a repeated offense. The number of days in custody before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days for each person. Wang Zhou Shi, Zhang Debiao, and Wu Zhiquan are given a two-year suspended sentence. Smoking paraphernalia and other items are confiscated and destroyed according to the list. Shen Wangshi is innocent.

▲Police Department versus Xia A'quan et al. for Opium Case (Ruling): Xia A'quan is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for providing premises for others to smoke opium. Yue Jinhua and Fang Guangbao are each sentenced to one month of imprisonment for smoking opium. The number of days in custody before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days for each person. Bao Guangbao is given a two-year suspended sentence. Smoking paraphernalia is confiscated.

▲Police Department versus Wang Jingui for Obstructing Public Duty Case (Ruling): Wang Jingui is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for the crime of obstructing public duty. A two-year suspended sentence is given.

▲Police Department versus Liang Jiubao for Gambling Case (Ruling): Liang Jiubao is sentenced to two months of imprisonment and fined sixty yuan for gathering people for gambling with the intention of profit. If he is unable to pay the fine, it will be converted to imprisonment at a rate of two yuan per day. The number of days in custody before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days. Gambling money and gambling paraphernalia are confiscated according to the list. (Above, October 3rd)

Shanghai Local Court 204

▲Civil Judgment: One judgment, Zhou Qinbao et al. versus He Gengxing, for debt dispute (Ruling): The defendant should repay the plaintiff principal and interest of 5,896.88 yuan in foreign currency. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant. One judgment, Xiechengchang Store versus Sun Guanlin et al., for debt arrears dispute (Ruling): Defendant Sun Guanlin should repay the original silver 746 taels and 7 qian 7 fen, with interest calculated at an annual rate of 24% from the date of the loan until the date of completion of execution. If unable to fulfill, Feng Zhongci and Zhang Wangdou are jointly and severally responsible for repayment. The plaintiff's remaining claims are rejected. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant Sun Guanlin.

The second instance litigation costs are borne by the appellant.

▲One Ruling, Zhang Guohua versus Huang Dianchen for Debt Pre-Seizure Case (Ruling): The movable property of the debtor located at No. 70 Jiangyin Street, inside Yuxingchang, up to the aforementioned claim amount of 330 yuan, should be pre-seized for the purpose of repayment. However, if the debtor provides security close to the aforementioned claim amount, they may apply to suspend or revoke the pre-seizure. The defendant Huang Dianchen should be notified accordingly.

▲One Judgment, Jiang Yongfa versus Ren Shunan for Bill Payment Dispute (Ruling): The Defendant should pay the Plaintiff bill amount of Silver one hundred twenty-one taels and six qian. Litigation costs are to be borne by the Defendant. Defendant Ren Shunan should be notified.

▲One Judgment, Yan Yang Shi versus Fan Jinfu et al. for Mortgage Payment Dispute (Ruling): Defendant Fan Jinfu should repay the Plaintiff a principal of two hundred fifty yuan in foreign currency, plus an interest of two hundred fifty yuan in foreign currency. If repayment is not possible, it shall be the responsibility of Yang Heting to repay on his behalf. Litigation costs are to be borne by Defendant Fan Jinfu.

▲One Judgment, Wang Shijia versus Teng Tianwen et al. for Debt Arrears Lawsuit (Ruling): Defendant Teng Tianwen should pay the Plaintiff a rental amount of one hundred twenty-seven yuan and six jiao in foreign currency. If payment is not possible, it shall be the responsibility of Lü Liming to pay on his behalf. Peng Xingfa should pay the Plaintiff a rental amount of one hundred thirty-three yuan, and shall vacate and return the house. Litigation costs are to be borne equally by Defendants Teng Tianwen and Peng Xingfa.

▲One Judgment, Zhuang Zhengxin versus Jie Jinxian for Rent Arrears Lawsuit (Ruling): The Defendant should repay the Plaintiff a rental amount of one hundred fifty yuan in foreign currency. Litigation costs are to be borne by the Defendant. (Above, October 3rd)
